29 Under its proportional system, voters elect senators and representatives rather independently of the candidates'
party affiliation, with politicians often migrating from one party to another. The high proportionality and the weak
affiliation of politicians to party institutions have made it more challenging to achieve fiscal discipline in Brazil
than in many other countries because under these institutions political consensus often requires a relaxation of fiscal
performance. Marcos Josd, "Incentivos Eletorais e Desequilibrio Fiscal de Estados e Municipios ", unpublished
mimeo, 1998, provides an extensive discussion of the impact of political institutions on fiscal performance. At
present, a political reform bill has been submitted to Congress to strengthen part affiliation.



46
programs or activities is difficult.30 These issues support the need for Brazil to carefully plan
how program managers will be integrated with program operations (or vice versa), as well the
need to develop deeper program evaluations which explore linkages between activities,
outcomes, and objectives.
124.  For introducing formal evaluations, international experience has indicated the importance
of formal and systematic linkages between evaluation results and the budget process. 31 The
Ministry of Planning has acknowledged the importance of integration, and has requested advice
on integrating evaluations into the budget process.
125.  The SIAFI 21st Century proposal is largely consistent with lessons learned in Brazil in
relation to the management of large governmental information systems, as well as with
international experiences in relation to the normal life cycle of integrated financial management
applications in the public sector.
126.  An important lessons learned are that systems have to be flexible to accommodate
various types of users, and that their technology must permit adaptation without major structural
changes or programming, to new legal and policy environments and to ever changing
institutional arrangements. The large centralized mainframe-system like the current SIAFI,
accessible only by terminal did not provide these facilities. Because of this, "management
version" of SIAFI had to be eventually implemented and there is not adequate and efficient
integration between its original and more recent subsystems. These and other lessons are being
taken into account for the design and development of the new SIAFI 21 st Century.
127.  The normal life span of IFMS systems in Latin-American countries comparable to
Brazil's size and complexity of their federal systems has been much less than SIAFI's 13 years
in operation. The Argentine SIDIF system was developed around 1992 and - similarly to SIAF1-
using computing languages and environments that even then were close to obsolescence, was
subject to comprehensive technological and functional modernization in the late nineties,
including the development of institutional or "local" SIDIF version to be implemented in
ministries and other entities finances with federal budget resources. In the case of Mexico, the
SIAF application developed and implemented in the federal treasury department in the early
nineties has been recently replaced by a new, more modem version.
RISKS AND RISK MITIGATION PROCEDURES
128.  The risks that the benefits of the program supported by the proposed operation might not
materialize can be discussed in terms of its different components. Risks could include: (i)
macroeconomic shocks with an adverse bearing on domestic interest rates, growth, and fiscal
performance; (ii) weak impact of the LFR with an adverse effect on fiscal planning or fiscal
execution; (iii) weak management of PPA programs, resulting in poor implementation and
evaluation of those programs; (iv) weak link of evaluation of PPA programs to program
budgeting and program management, resulting in low gains in terms of allocational and technical
efficiency and of service delivery to the public; (v) SIAFI; (vi) inadequate consensus on
30 "Integrating Financial Management and Performance Management." OECD PUMA, July 1999. P. 9.
31 "Improving Evaluation Practices: Best Practices Guidelines for Evaluation and Background Paper." OECD
PUMA. January 1999. P. 27.



47
completion of administrative reform, with and adverse bearing on personnel costs, on personnel
management, and on the quality of service delivery.
129.  Macroeconomic Shocks. Brazil's economic performance is subject to external and
domestic shocks, particularly those emerging from changes in interest rates and changes in
public expenditures. Three possible risks are discussed:
* Deterioration of fiscal Performance due to higher interest rates. The effects of an
exogenous increase in interest rates (due, for example, to reduced international investor in
emerging markets), are considered first. First, the direct effect of an interest rate increase on
fiscal performance is discussed. Under a standard fiscal sustainability accounting framework,
the effect can be measured by the impact on the end-year debt to GDP ratio in 2001 of an
increase of one percentage point in the average real interest rate of the year. Given the
assumptions on other key variables of the fiscal sustainability framework (GDP
growth=4.5%; primary balance=3%), the effect is an increase of 0.3 of a percentage point in
the debt/GDP ratio. This effect would be offset by an increase of about 0.35 of a percentage
point in the annual primary surplus (as a percentage of GDP). This means that Brazil can
manage annual real interest increases of up to about three percentage points in the real annual
interest rate with an increase of one percentage point in the primary surplus. Since the onset
of the Fiscal Stability Plan, Brazil has demonstrated its ability to implement changes in the
primary surplus of that magnitude and more.
-  Deterioration of arowth due to hi2her interest rates. Second, the impact of an increase in
interest rates on output is considered. Recent work by the IMF has addressed this question in
the context of a vector autoregression model that traces the effects of monetary shocks that
result from an changes in the SELIC rate.32 The effect is described as powerful and
persistent, with the impact of a two standard-deviation increase in the annual SELIC rate (an
increase of about 4 percentage points) leading to a decline in output of up to almost 1%
within about seven months. These measurements point not only to the power of monetary
policy but also to the risks of other exogenous factors that might raise (or lead the authorities
to raise) interest rates. However, based on the recent experience in Brazil, such a shock,
while disruptive, would also be likely to cause Brazilian authorities to undertake fiscal
adjustments to offset or reduce the fiscal impact of increased rates. This fiscal adjustment
could have an additional temporary adverse effect on the growth rate, lasting while the policy
response works its way to reduce debt, help enhance confidence and lower interest rates.
*  Impact of higher spendin2 on the current account. Third, the effect of higher govermnent
spending financed by higher debt is analyzed. Recent work by the IMF has also addressed
this question, this time in using their dynamic multicountry macro model (MULTIMOD)33.
In this model, increased spending affects private savings and investment, and the current
account through higher government absorption and higher risk premia on Brazilian financial
instruments. The real would depreciate in real terms because the positive impact on the real
exchange rate (defined as reais per dollar) of higher risk premia would more than offset the
negative impact of increased government absorption. This would initially improve the current
account. However, the positive impact on net exports would eventually fade away and the
final outcome would be deterioration of the CAD and a higher level of net foreign liabilities.
32 See IMF, Brazil - Selected Issues and Statistical Appendix, SM/00/25 1, November 10, 2000, Section VII.
33 See IMF, ibid., Section X.



48
The effects generated by the MULTIMOD simulations run over several years. The risk that
the shock that triggers this scenario materializes is contained by the strengthened fiscal
policy framework, where increases in expenditures are restricted by the stronger budget
constraints being faced by governments and by the provisions of the Law of Fiscal
Responsibility.
130. The Law of Fiscal Responsibilit . A low impact of the LFR could result from weak
incentives for fiscal responsibility, including weaknesses of LFR remedies. One critical factor
here is the strength of budget constraints faced by the public sector. A relaxed budget constraint,
in terms of a relaxed access to credit, would weaken the relevance of the LFR, as governments
would plan on expanding expenditures with additional borrowing, leading to increased
indebtedness. The risk of relaxing budget constraints is contained by Brazil's commitment to low
inflation and by current levels of debt that are already high by historical standards. Brazil's
commitment to low inflation means that it would bot be politically rewarding to risk fiscal
instability resulting in monetary expansion. High levels of debt mean that access to new debt is
costly and that service on existing debt is already a heavy burden on public budgets. Higher
indebtedness would further increase cost or reduce access, and further worsen the burden of debt
service on public budgets. Both these factors (commitment to low inflation and high debt levels)
suggest that the budget constraint faced by Brazil's government is likely to be stronger than in
the past.
131.  A second critical factor is weak enforcement of the LFR. Weak enforcement may result
due to (i) the exclusion of voluntary transfers for health and education from the prohibition to
provide voluntary transfers to those governments that do not comply with key LFR provisions to
with an adverse effect on fiscal planning or fiscal execution; (ii) the low share of new credit in
the revenues of many governments (new credit is another remedy for non-compliance with key
LFR provisions; and (iii) inadequate monitoring/prosecution of non-compliance with LFR
provisions with penal implications under the Law of Fiscal Crimes. The exclusion referred to in
(i) above indeed means that the voluntary transfers remedy will not be a critical factor
determining the success of the LFR (although, as discussed before, some governments are
reacting positively to the possibility of its application). Similarly, the ban of credit will be
irrelevant to the many governments that borrow little. Nevertheless, for some governments that
are envisaging new credit operations to finance critical investment projects, the credit remedies
likely to encourage compliance with the LFR. Finally, on (iii) above, there is the perception that
penal legislation is an important deterrent to official misconduct, and that the strength of such a
deterrent has been increasing. Indeed, recent data on dismissals by reason of misconduct have
shown a significant increase over the last few years. It is believed that such a rise responds more
to better monitoring and prosecution than to a higher propensity for misconduct.
132.  The Multiannual Plan. There are risks to PPA's sustainability and to achievement of its
full potential. These include
* political change, or the risk that the reform may weaken during an incoming administration,
or simply ignored and left to decay. To mitigate this risk, the Ministry of Planning is using a
strategy of gradual implementation of PPA, emphasizing the benefits of data for management
improvement rather then initially emphasizing only accountability.
* bureaucratic resistance, or the risk the reforms will be actively opposed or simply ignored
by the bureaucracy, thereby undermining the success of the PPA initiatives (e.g. performance



49
management, improving program management, coordinating with other activities, use of
evaluation results, and reflecting program priorities in budgets and program implementation).
Threats to the bureaucracy are also being downplayed in terms of elimination of duplicative
activities. Initially, this is being left to Ministries to identify and address (e.g. reallocation of
these resources to other areas). If this does not succeed, at some future date, the Ministry of
Planning may initiate steps to eliminate duplication.
* change management, or the risk that Congress, in particular, is not able to quickly adapt to
the new program format and means of making budget choices, and thus reject the change
entirely, or require simultaneous transmittal of the proposed budget in the old format. The
speed with which the new format is adopted and used is partially influenced by Ministry of
Planning or Executive branch efforts to explain and train external groups on the use and
interpretation of the new format. Similar concerns arise relative to line Ministries and
Departments
* PPA integration in the budget, or the risks that resource allocation or budget execution be
impervious to evaluation. This risk will begin to be tested next year, when Congress approves
the LDO for the 2002 budget, which should reflect the evaluation presently being conducted.
A related risk is that the absence of full-cost accounting undermine transparency and lead to
poor policy decisions because of misrepresentation of resources allocated to programs and
the relationship of staff costs to program outcomes. Integration of PPA into the budget would
be part of the technical assistance project that is under preparation.
* program manager integration into program operations, or the risk that, given their
limited role, programs managers be unable to influence activity managers to cooperate or
achieve the full potential productivity gains from coordinating activities linked into
programs.
Any of these may reduce the effectiveness of PPA, and lead to its revision or abandonment. But,
there are threats faced by any public sector reform effort in any country. The Ministry of
Planning is aware of these issues, and is atternpting to manage risks and improve the probability
of PPA's success.
133.  For integration of program managers into program operations, the Ministry of Planning is
deliberately not pressing this issue immediately, to reduce threats to the bureaucracy. However,
the Ministry is contemplating additional reforms to strengthen the role of program managers,
including the possibility of channeling resources through program managers, who would then
"contract" with the Ministry departments and activities.
134. The Integrated Financial Managiement System. Like any large systems development
project, SIAFI 21st Century faces important implementation and completion risks, for which
there are a number of equally important mitigating factors.
Technological risks
135.  From the technological standpoint, consideration is being given to models, platforms,
environments and development techniques and tools which represent a dramatic departure from
those prevailing since the current SIAFI system was developed and implemented some 13 years
ago. This will have major effects on information resources both, during project execution and
later for post-implementation maintenance. System users will be migrating from a character



50
mode interface environment to a graphic mode Windows environment, and to an internet
environment. System availability for 24 hours per day, 7 days per week, while being a benefit,
will also represent work scheduling challenges both for information resources and users.
136.  However, technological risks are mitigated by the careful approach being taken by both,
the STN and SERPRO in terms of validating technological alternatives and choices through
extensive pilot testing at each of the three proposed system layers (data, application and user
interface) with the support of external consultants and the participation of potential suppliers of
goods and services. Other mitigating factors include current training of information resources in
the use of the design and development tools that will be used in the construction of applications,
as well as plans to provide extensive training to users of the systems before the various
subsystems become operational. Another consideration is that while the technology being
considered is new in a SIAFI environment, there is substantial successful experience with it, both
internationally and in Brazil. Finally, SERPRO has a very solid and longstanding experience as
a developer and operator of government systems in Brazil, including the development of the
current SIAFI system and its operation during the past 13 years, thus it is familiar with the
Brazilian legal framework and rules of the business for public sector financial management at all
federal government levels.
Political and financing risks
137.  The risk of changes in political priorities are always higher in the case of multiannual
projects requiring high levels of investment. Technological risks may materialize producing
delays and cost overruns in project implementation which could result in a loss of political favor
and of completion funding. Coordination between project completion and the budgeting and
financial schedules may be lost because of technological or funding delays, resulting in project
implementation breakdowns. General economic and financial conditions may force a
government to cut down on new and ongoing projects. A new administration may decide to
pursue a different approach for a project that has high-profile incidence over government
management systems, transparency and accountability.
138.  Notwithstanding these and other completion risks, the SIAFI 21"t Century project is
being proposed not only as a much needed technological development in view of the increasing
obsolescence of the current SIAFI, but it is also supported on major policy actions, such as the
PPA and the Fiscal Responsibility Law (LRF), which are key components of the current
administration's program. The project is scheduled to be completed during the current
administration's term in office. Being instrumental to facilitate monitoring and evaluation of
performance under the PPA and the LRF, it is likely to remain funded until completion, though
implementation delays taking completion beyond the current administration's term could have
less predictable effects. The project's implementation schedule is based on the gradual
completion and implementation of its various subsystems and modules, thus there is built-in
flexibility to establish development priorities in coordination with budgeting and financial fiscal
year schedules. The fact that subsystems or modules of the current SIAFI will continue operating
as needed during the implementation of the project substantially mitigates the risk of financial
management breakdowns.
139.  In summary, while SIAFI 21t Century faces the various types of implementation and
completion risks inherent to a project of its type and scope, there are also important mitigating



51
factors that support its viability, among which stand out the very conservative approach of STN
and SERPRO for the validation of technological alternatives and the fact that the project falls
within the framework of major policy initiatives such as the PPA and the LRF.
140.  Debt Managzement. The major risk of the debt management component is that the
program be unable to achieve a reduction on the current vulnerability of the debt portfolio, in
particular the refinancing and interest rate risks. The institutionalization of a sound debt
management practice, that incorporates a risk management framework (ALM), could face two
risks: (i) changes in the macroeconomic and market conditions make the effort an extremely
expensive and difficult challenge to pursue; (ii) the project is not properly supported and
consolidated within the Ministry of Finance and as a result becomes ineffective.
141.  In the first case, changes in the external macroeconomic conditions, manifested in the
market's willingness to purchase longer term and/or fixed rate instruments, could reduce or
neutralize the effect of the project on reducing the vulnerability of the debt portfolio. However,
the existence of a well-structured organizational capacity properly supported on the policy side
would reduce the size of the impact of such macroeconomic change.
142.  In the second case, the risk is that the proposed institutional and organizational changes
do not achieve a critical mass. As a result, proper governance structure, such as a debt
management committee and a portfolio benchmark, does not get formally sanctioned by the
Minister. The Treasury is not able to create a sustainable and credible structure to really guide
and implement the new policies. The credibility of the Treasury as a capable manager of the debt
relies mostly on the capacity to maintain a well qualified and motivated group of managers and,
to a less degree but also important, to provide managers access to the analytical and operational
tools which allows them to execute their tasks properly and efficiently. The risk that institutional
changes do not achieve a critical mass is mitigated by (i) the fact that many key changes have
taken place or are on the way to taking place without signs of lack of government commitment;
(ii) the authorities are aware, given the size of Brazil's bonded debt of the strong need for good
debt management that will contain risks and long term costs. Therefore, the risk that the
authorities would let the program or reforms to weaken or slow down is small.



52

and recommend that the Executive Directors approve it.

ANNEX 1: LETTER OF SECTOR DEVELOPMENT POLICY
Brasilia, December 20, 2000
Mr. James D. Wolfensohn
President
The World Bank
Washington, DC
Dear Mr. Wolfensohn:
This letter of sector policy discusses progress in the economic program of the Brazilian
Government, including main developments in its fiscal, public expenditure and debt management
policy framework. We request financial assistance from IBRD, in the form of a programmatic
public sector adjustment loan and in support of the implementation of these policies. Brazil's
Fiscal, Public Expenditure, and Federal Debt Management Reforms are central components of
the Government's reform program. We believe they constitute important initiatives of the
Brazilian Government to be supported by the Bank under a programmatic adjustment loan.
Macroeconomic Outcomes and Prospects
The Economy from 1997 through 2000
2.    Brazil has achieved its macroeconomic targets in the last few years and looks towards the
future with a solid basis for sustained growth. The economy has shown resilience to external
shocks and has registered increases in production and employment within a context of decreasing
inflation. Real GDP growth is expected to reach 4 percent in 2000 and all major forecasts point
to rates of four percent and over in the years ahead. Unemployment declined to 6.7 percent last
September from 7.4 percent in September 1999 in a context of a strong reentry in labor market.
Inflation has remained subdued despite external shocks, particularly high oil prices. There are
solid grounds to achieve the 6 per cent central inflation target for 2000. Moreover, the
Government has already announced a 4 per cent target for 2001 and 3.5 per cent target for 2002,
with a two percentage points margin. These targets are in accordance with commitments made
within the context of MERCOSUR.
3.    Strict fiscal discipline has been maintained at all levels of government and constitutes the
best guarantee for solid non-inflationary future growth. Brazil registered a 3.23 percent of GDP
primary surplus in 1999 and is committed to produce a 3.1 percent surplus at year end 2000.
From January to October, the overall public sector primary surplus, encompassing the Federal
government and the Central Bank, States and Municipalities and public enterprises, reached 3.25
percent of GDP. The public sector borrowing requirement has decreased from 5.75 percent of
GDP in December 1999 to 4.13 percent last October. The Federal government performance has
been the main force behind positive fiscal results, showing a primary surplus of 2.6 percent of
GDP from January to September 2000. But States and Municipalities' results have also seen an
important turnaround. Since mid 1999 they have shifted from permanent deficits to positive



54
results. States and Municipalities' primary surplus from January to October reached 0.52 percent
of GDP against a 0.23 percent in December 1999. This is the result of a solid implementation of
the agreements reached between the Federal government and 25 States as well as with 180
Municipalities, including all the largest Municipalities. The fiscal result of State enterprises has
also remained strong, with the production of a 0.88 primary surplus between January and
October 2000, against a 0.64 percent surplus in December 1999. As a consequence of reforms
introduced in the social security system of private workers, the social security deficit has halted a
trend of permanent deficit increases. From 1999 to 2000 the deficit has been kept stable at R$
6.7 billion. The budget for 2001, submitted to Congress forecasts a primary surplus of R$ 28 .1
billion, consistent with the consolidated target of 3% of GDP. At the same time, a target for
2002 was set at 2.7% of GDP.
4.    Despite the stringent fiscal efforts, the Government has successfully protected key social
expenditures. In the 2000 budget, twenty two priority programs in education, health, labor and
social assistance were protected, all of them treated in the context of previous IDB and World
Bank structural loans. At the same time, the Federal government is implementing a program to
improve the quality and focus of spending in the social area. The first positive results in health
and education were shown in the Pesquisa Nacional de Amostragem por Domicilio - PNAD
(National Household Sample Survey) of 1999, released by the Brazilian Institute of Geography
and Statistics (IBGE) in July 2000. Moreover, a new important initiative - Programa Alvorada
- was launched, to support income growth in areas with human development index below the
national average. In December 2000, following a Senate deliberation, the House approved in a
first round a constitutional amendment establishing the Poverty Combat Fund.
5.    The Brazilian privatization program has been following its course. A major recent event
in December 1999 was the privatization of BANESPA, the largest State bank, sold to Banco
Santander for US$ 3.5 billion. FDI, of which privatization is only a small portion, achieved US$
29.9 billion in 1999 and US$ 22.9 billion from January to October 2000. The expectation is that
for the calendar year 2000, FDI will reach an amount between US$ 25 billion and US$ 30
billion, more than enough to finance the current account deficit, that is expected to amount to
approximnately US$ 25 billion.
The Government's Fiscal, Public Expenditure and Debt Management Programs
6.    A number of important structural reforms were undertaken recently covering the fiscal
area, debt management and the budgetary process. Such reforms are the best guarantee for a
solid and healthy economic performance in the years ahead. What follows is a brief description
of the main features of the reforms.
Fiscal Management
7.    A historical milestone of Brazilian Fiscal Reform Program is the approval of the Fiscal
Responsibility Law (Lei de Responsabilidade Fiscal - LRF) by the Brazilian Congress.
Establishing a code for the behavior of the public administrator, the LRF sets forth the principles,
rules and limits that provide for a responsible fiscal management at Federal, State and Municipal
levels. Planning, prudence, transparency and accountability in the management of public funds
by the Executive, Legislative and Judicial Branches are promoted, making the LRF one of the
main instruments for the long term sustainability of the fiscal adjustment.
8.    Limits for personnel expenditures and for public debt, as well as the obligation to set
fiscal targets (on revenues, expenditures, nominal and primary balances, and debt) are



55
established or required, with special provisions for electoral years. The Law also provides for
corrective measures when fiscal targets, expenditure limits or debt limits are not met. Increased
transparency and electronic dissemination of information to the public are also provided for in
the Law and constitute one of it main objectives. Moreover, the Law prohibits intergovernmental
lending and the refinancing of debt of any of the three levels of Government by the others.
Together with a set of measures in the relationship of the Federal Government with States and
Municipalities, comprising among others the privatization of public banks and the debt
rescheduling agreements, these prohibitions are among the most important steps taken to change
the face of the Country's fiscal regime.
9.    The Fiscal Responsibility Crimes Law (Lei de Crimes de Responsabilidade Fiscal -
LCRF), approved by Congress on the second half of this year, constitutes a fundamental
complement to the LRF. It introduces penal sanctions, in addition to the institutional sanctions
already provided for in the LRF, such as suspension of transfers of funds and of contracting
credit operations. Therefore, all public administrators in charge of activities related to a sound
fiscal policy may now be personally punished by, among others penalties, fines and even
imprisonment, in case of mismanagement of its fiscal duties.
10.   These important steps, however, are a beginning. A new challenge, as important as
adopting the laws, is implementation. The Brazilian Federal Government is fully commnitted
with this objective and is carrying out actions aimed at promoting and supporting their
implementation. In this context, within the timeframe provided for in the LRF, a draft regulation
establishing limits for Federal bonded debt and a draft law creating the Fiscal Management
Council (Conselho de Gestdo Fiscal) were submitted to Congress and a draft regulation setting
the limits for the public consolidated debt (comprising Federal, States and Municipal
governments) was submitted to the Senate.
11.   The implementation of the LRF at sub-national level is of fundamental importance.
Under the LRF, States and Municipalities are expected to improve their fiscal performance
through befter planning, management and transparency. In particular, fiscal planning will provide
for the preparation of fiscal target and fiscal risk annexes to budget guidelines laws (leis de
diretrizes orcamentarias) introduced by all levels of government except municipalities with a
population below 50.000 inhabitants. Also, fiscal management will include high frequency
reporting on budget outcomes and compliance with targets. The Federal Government is taking
the necessary steps to promote the follow up, consolidation and analysis of data to be generated
by States and Municipalities, comprising the information on targets, risks, fiscal management,
and fiscal accounts required by the law. It will also monitor sub-national debt levels and provide
for making the information on such levels available to the public. The consolidated reports on
States and Municipalities will constitute important tools to evaluate the fiscal policy in Brazil
and the effectiveness of the LRF. The Brazilian Government has initiated conversations with the
Bank seeking its support to a technical assistance project that will  help develop LRF
implementation at sub-national level and allow a comprehensive analysis of the perspectives and
risks for the public sector based on the budget guidelines laws (leis de diretrizes orqamentarias)
for 2002 to be adopted by States and Municipalities. The initial stage of the project will be
limited to a small number of Municipalities.
12.   In terms of outcomes, the LRF will help sustain fiscal adjustment at the sub-national
level, where, as noted before, the primary surplus increased considerably. As a result of the
improved fiscal performance, sub-national net debt levels (as a percent of net revenues) have



56
been stabilized and are likely to remain so or decline during 2001-02. Together with the
declining debt revenue ratio at the federal level, these developments at the sub-national level are
expected to encourage private sector investment and growth, a key condition to further reduce
poverty rates.
Public Expenditure Management
PPA
13.   The Brazilian Constitution requires the President to present to Congress every four years
a Pluriannual Plan (PPA) with the government plan and targets for the next four years. The PPA
for 2000-2003 (called Avan,a Brasil) presented on August 31, 1999 by President Cardoso, and
approved by Congress, sets a new paradigm for government planning and defines the strategic
orientation for the government, aiming at consolidating the economic stability while promoting
sustainable growth and development, employment and income generation, fighting poverty and
social exclusion, strengthening democracy and protecting human rights, reducing regional
discrepancies and promoting minorities' rights.
14.   A study carried out by a consulting firm, under the supervision of the Ministry of
Planning, Budget and Management and the National Bank for Economic and Social
Development, identifying the National Integration and Development Regions (Eixos Nacionais
de Integra,do e Desenvolvimento), listed the social and economic investment opportunities, with
special attention to their contribution to regional integration. After an innovative and
comprehensive process of consultations with the general public and sub-national governments
all over the Country, a group of 388 programs were identified by the Federal Government.
These programs form the PPA, covering all actions of the Federal Government, including
investments in areas such as energy, transportation, telecommunications, social development,
environment, information and knowledge, to be carried out in partnership with the private sector,
whenever feasible.
15.   Ultimately, the PPA approach will contribute to improve the delivery of public services.
An important PPA program - Programa Qualidade no Servi,o PuTblico, or Public Service
Quality Program - aims to achieve a 70% satisfaction rate by 2003 among customers of
governmental agencies that adhere to the program (1200 thus far with the aim of reaching 3000
by 2002). Other PPA programs with a focus on improved service delivery include the Program to
Reduce Bureaucracy (Programa de Desburocratiza,do), with 420 measures already enacted, and
a results oriented Public Management Program (Programa Gestao Puiblica Empreendedora).
Under these programs, the streamlining of public institutions is aimed at, with focus on better
serving the citizens, establishing regulatory agencies, with self-sustainable and flexible
management structures, as well as supporting new entities with private administration and public
purposes, to enhance the cooperation between public and private sector. Additionally, targets for
2003, timetables and monitoring indicators were set and are available to the public. The
Government will annually monitor the programs to identify those that are on track.
16.   The PPA sets the conditions for a better integration of the planning instruments available
to the Federal Government: the PPA itself, the Budget Guidelines Law and the Budget Law. The
draft Budget Law for 2001 presented to Congress changes a 25 years practice of functional
budgetary allocation (classifica~do funcional-programatica) and incorporates the concept of
"programs", with their respective targets and indicators. It shall pave the way for more
efficiency, better quality and enhanced transparency of public expenditures. Presently, the
Ministry of Planning, Budget and Managernent is conducting a general evaluation of programs



57
and their management, with inputs from program managers and from the corresponding sector
ministries. Such an evaluation will facilitate the identification of priority programs to be
included in the draft 2002 Budget Guidelines Law, which will be submitted to Congress in April
2001. The evaluation itself will also be sent to Congress. The definition of priority programs, for
which the Government intends to ensure full budget execution, is a key tool of the Government's
budgetary and development policy.
17.   The change in planning is followed by a change in management. Based on the successful
experience of the Brasil em Aqao Program (1996-1999), a new management process was adopted
to promote entrepreneurial behavior. For each program a manager was appointed and trained.
This represents a major departure from long-standing and well-established practices and
behavior within Brazil's public sector. It is necessary to provide the managers with the abilities
and tools required for the successful completion of their tasks. In this regard, a management
information system (SIG) has been established but needs to be improved. The improvement
involves among other steps providing internet access to the public. Access will complement the
existing AvanCa Brasil and Infra-estrutura websites, will enhance PPA transparency and
visibility and will strengthen the sustainability of the PPA process. A training program for
program teams will be implemented during 2001-02 Moreover, for a better integration of the
planning process, it is necessary to improve the programs' performance evaluation mechanisms
and the framework in which they will feedback, together with other factors, into the budget.
The Government expects to implement this effort during 2001 with the Bank's support, under
the above referred technical assistance project.
SIAFI 21't Century
18.   Since 1987 the Federal Government Financial Administration Integrated System (SIAFI)
has been operating. At that time it was a state of the art system that inspired several sub-national
and even foreign systems. SIAFI nowadays integrates more than four thousand units of the
Executive, Legislative and Judiciary Branches, including the indirect administration, and offers
total transparency regarding the uses and sources of public funds. Presently, more than fifty
thousand transactions are registered daily in the system, of which about 30% refer to payments
made, including all relevant data.
19.   After several expansions and additions and in the context of the improvements already
promoted in the public expenditure management, the Federal Government considers it is time to
adopt a new mechanism, consistent with the challenges of the new century. The project SIAFI
21st Century is being conceived as a response to the necessity of including new features to and
updating the technological basis of the system. Among the new features to be incorporated are:
web interface, to create a more user friendly environment; 24 hour/ day and 7 days/week
availability; increased number of simultaneous accesses; increased transparency, through an
internet gateway public information center (Portal SIAFI); budgetary planning, to further
facilitate and improve the interface with the budget; effective expenditures control, with costs
appropriation by administrative unit and program; and integrated register and control of the
stocks and flows of the National Treasury's assets and liabilities, including internal and external
debt. Additionally, the new system will have enhanced reporting capabilities and will allow
monitoring the financial condition of States and Municipalities. The new system will be an
important tool for the National Treasury to better perform its role, addressing its main needs
regarding its operations and the management of Federal finances, budget and debt, under the new
Law of Fiscal Responsibility and the PPA framework. Implementation of the SIAFI 2lt Century
project has already begun with the initial development of its five modules (financial



58
management, budget management, monitoring of States and Municipalities, public debt
management and re-engineering of treasury operations). The Government expects to complete
most of the implementation of these modules by 2002. Contact with the Bank has been initiated,
aiming at its support under the referred technical assistance project. The support could cover
advice and assistance in technological and implementation management, as well as cost-
effectiveness issues.
Administrative Reform
20.   Fully aware of the importance of a modern public administration to support sustainable
growth and economic stabilization, the Brazilian Government is promoting a comprehensive
reform of the public administration. Several measures have been adopted in the last few years,
including constitutional changes to redefine the role of the state and allow for more flexibility in
dealing with personnel issues. Among these measures and in addition to the new management
system for public programs referred to above, more than 100 thousand public positions were
closed, a draft law was proposed to Congress in order to regulate the dismissal of public
employees based on insufficient performance and a strict salary increase policy has been adopted
and thoroughly implemented. Administrative Reform has been a key tool to help contain
personnel expenditures, which, under the Fiscal Responsibility Law, will be limited to 50% of
net revenues at the Federal Government level and to 60% of net revenues in States and
Municipalities by 2001.
Debt Management
21.   The Government has given renewed attention to improving debt management. A new
institutional arrangement, consistent with the Brazilian public administration practices is being
developed, taking into account the worldwide trends. The first concrete measure is the
proposition, within the National Treasury's structure, of three units - modeled as front, middle
and back offices, with the responsibility for short term strategy dealing with primary bond
issuance, for the development of public debt's  long term strategy and relationship with
investors; and for federal public debt's registration, control, budgetary and financial
programming, payments and statistics.
22.   These new institutional arrangements are made in the framework of transference, to the
National Treasury, of the duties carried out by the Central Bank, such as bond issuance in the
domestic market for monetary policy purposes and management of external liabilities, including
bond issuance in the foreign market. On the domestic side, such transference process is well
advanced. Central Bank activities are now limited to advising the National Treasury and issuing
domestic debt denominated in foreign currency. On May 4, 2002, as provided in the Fiscal
Responsibility Law, the Central Bank will no longer be authorized to issue securities in the
internal market and will have to ask the Treasury to proceed to any issuing associated with the
execution of monetary policy. Issuance of bond in the foreign markets will be carried out by the
National Treasury in due time.
23.   The central objectives of debt management are: (i) to extend the average maturity of
domestic debt issues, (ii) to reduce refinancing risks, (iii) to reduce the cost of borrowing taking
into account adequate risk level, (iv) to gradually increase the duration of debt and reduce
foreign currency denominated bonded debt, (v) to develop and consolidate an yield curve in the
domestic market of securities with a prefixed rate and indexed to IGP-M, and (vi) to improve the
secondary market for public sector securities. Through these efforts, the maximum maturity of



59
domestic bonds has already increased from the previous benchmark of 3 months to 24 months. In
international placements, a successful forty- year issue was recently made
24.   Several other measures have also been adopted with regard to debt management: (i)
beginning in 2001, an Annual Borrowing Plan, with the objectives, strategies and expectations
for each fiscal year, will be made available to the public; (ii) establishment of an unit within the
National Treasury with the sole purpose of assessing and quantifying contingent liabilities; (iii)
establishment of annual limits for foreign loans to be contracted or guaranteed by the Federal
Government; and (iv) proposals of draft resolutions and law, to the Senate and to Congress
House, respectively, setting borrowing limits for Federal, State and Municipal Governments, as
well as for the Federal bond issuance.
25.   Notwithstanding the progress already made, it is necessary to further seek the
development of primary and secondary markets, the establishment of a benchmark curve for
Federal bonds in the domestic market, and the consolidation of Brazil's image as sovereign
issuer in the main international markets. For those purposes, additional actions are to be
implemented such as (i) consolidating the National Treasury's organizational structure; (ii)
strengthening National Treasury's governance, with better guidelines and procedures and with
clearer delegation and accountability framework ; (iii) development and improvement of risk
analysis and portfolio management tools; (iv) improvement and integration of existing
information systems; and (v) development of studies with the objective of establishing
benchmarks and medium term funding strategy.
Request for Financial Assistance
The Government remains firmly committed to its program of reforms as outlined above,
and would welcome World Bank financial assistance. We appreciate the prompt consideration of
the first US$ 750 million Programmatic Fiscal Reform Structural Adjustment Loan, in support of
the measures that have been enacted and are under implementation. We look forward to working
together with the Bank on a proposed future loan as further fiscal, public expenditure and debt
management reforms take place.
Yours sincerely,
Martus Tavares                       Pedro Sampaio Malan
Minister of Planning, Budget                Minister of Finance
And Management

ANNEX 4: BRAziL's NEW FIsCAL CODE
1.    In May, 2000, Brazil's Congress approved a new fiscal code known as the Law of Fiscal
Responsibility (Lei Complementar No. 101). The Law partly addresses Article 163 of the
Constitution, which requires issuance of a complementary law (i.e. a law intended to provide
detail on constitutional provisions and requiring only a simple majority for approval) regulating
public finance, public debt and guarantees, issuance and redemption of public bonds, inspection
of financial institutions, exchange rate operations by public agencies, and functions of public
financial institutions. The LFR covers public finance and debt. It does not regulate the budget
process, which is covered by Article 165 (9, II) of the constitution. The budget process is
presently regulated by Law 4320 of 1964. This annex provides a brief perspective with regard to
the impact of institutions on fiscal performance, describes the main components of the LFR,
evaluates how Brazilian fiscal institutions have been strengthened by issuance of the law and
other provisions, indicates the possible impact of the law on Brazil's fiscal sustainability, and
points to the risks in the successful implementation of the law.
Political Institutions
2.    The study of the impact of institutional factors on fiscal performance follows two
different strands of thought. One refers to the impact of political institutions; the other, to the
impact of budgetary institutions.  With regard to the impact of political institutions, the
hypotheses that have been tested in international comparisons suggest a strong link of political
stability (normally measured by the frequency of government changes) to fiscal performance,
with shorter government duration having an adverse impact on fiscal performance. Although
causation can go both ways, the argument can be made at the theoretical level, that governments
with too short a life have reduced incentives to undertake sustainable fiscal policies, as the
benefits of sustainability are reaped well beyond their terms in office.
3.    If it were as simple as indicated above, it would be easy to argue that Brazil's has good
political conditions for fiscal stability: a well-established democracy, with a standard length of a
government duration. But the politics of fiscal consensus are more complex than the simple
relationship indicated above. As an example of the further complexity, recent political analyses
argue (i) that a large number of representatives per district encourages proportional
representation, multiparty systems and coalition or minority governments; while (ii) "first-past-
the-post systems" (i.e., "systems where only one representative is elected per district and all
seats go to the winner") encourage two-party systems. As political systems move towards large
numbers of representatives per district, countries gain a higher degree of proportionality in
representation but are likely to have less decisive governments due to a weaker support in a more
polarized congress.
4.    Brazil's political system is one of proportional representation, with three senators per
state, at least eight representatives per municipality, and five major parties. But Brazil's system
has a further feature with a bearing on fiscal performance. Under its proportional system, voters
elect senators and representatives rather independently of the candidates' party affiliation, with
politicians often migrating from one party to another. The high proportionality and the weak



68
affiliation of politicians to party institutions have made it more challenging to achieve fiscal
discipline in Brazil than in many other countries because under these institutions political
consensus often requires a relaxation of fiscal performance. 34
Budget Institutions
5.     But fiscal outcomes also depend critically on budgetary institutions. At an empirical
level, much research in the European Union, the USA, and Latin America, have found important
effects of fiscal institutions on fiscal performance. For example, the level of stringency of
balanced budget rules in US has a negative effect on state deficits. Also, in Latin America,
"...countries with a high index of budget institutions tend to have lower deficits and lower debt
levels than countries with a low index of budget institutions."35
6.     Following recent Bank work on Brazil36, key budget institutions for aggregate fiscal
discipline can be classified as follows (i) ex-ante constraints; (ii) dominance of central budget
agencies; (iii) ex-ante agreements; (iv) multi-annual macroeconornic programs, (iv) numerical
limits. The effectiveness of these institutions depends on the extent to which the budget covers
all public sector activities (budget comprehensiveness); the exte;nt to which expenditures are not
autonomously driven (budget flexibility); the extent to which the budget covers revenues and
expenditures for the whole period for which it is approved (i.e. restraints on supplementary
budgets); the strength of budget constraints on sub-national governments and SOEs (i.e. no
bailing out or intergovernmental credit); the adequacy of the education and tenure of key
decision makers; and the strength of transparency and accountability, as determined by the
strength of auditing, ex-post reconciliation, sanctions, information, freedom of press, democracy,
education, and financial openness. With the effectiveness conditions listed above present, the
decision makers can formulate and implement valid primary balance and debt targets that are
consistent with fiscal discipline. It is in this area of budgetary institutions that Brazil has been
making major progress in its institutional conditions for aggregate fiscal discipline.
The Law of Fiscal Responsibility and the Law of Fiscal Crimes
7.     Brazil's new  Law  of Fiscal Responsibility (LFR) covers fiscal planning, budget
programming, budget execution, debt, credit, guarantees, net worth, transparency, and control.
The main provisions of the new law are described as follows:
*  The new law introduces planning of key fiscal variables in Brazil's budget legislation. The
federal and sub-national governments must now indicate, in the annual laws that regulate
budget programming, three-year targets with respect to revenues, expenditures, the primary
deficit and debt. Indication of these targets reflects federal fiscal policy since 1998. In 1998,
the federal government announced a fiscal stability plan for the public sector that has been
implemented rigorously. With the new law, the fiscal planning introduced by that plan has
been institutionalized and its scope deepened to sub-national governments.
34 Marcos Jose, "Incentivos Eletorais e Desequilibrio Fiscal de Estados e Municipios ", unpublished mimeo, 1998,
provides an extensive discussion of the impact of political institutions o fiscal performance. At present, a political
reform bill has been submitted to Congress to strengthen part affiliation.
3 See Stein, E., Talvi, E., and Grisanti, A. "Institutional Arrangements and Fiscal Performance" The Latin
American Experience", mimeo, Inter-American Development Bank, published in www.iadb.org.
36 Brazil, Structural Reform for Fiscal Sustainabilitv, report No. 19593-BR.



69
*  Under the LFR, governments must indicate contingent liabilities and the policies to be taken
in case those liabilities materialize.
*  Fiscal execution must limit expenditure commitments when revenues fall below target.
Revenues and expenditures are monitored through a publicly disclosed and disseminated bi-
monthly report. Compliance with targets are monitored through a fiscal management report
issued every four months.
*  Expenditures are subject to (i) consistency with PPAs and LDOs; (ii) net increases in
permanent expenditures (expenditures legally mandated for more than two years) not to
exceed increases in permanent revenues; (iii) limits on personnel expenditures revenues
(50% for the federal government; 60% for states and municipalities) and on the distribution
of those ceilings among branches of government37; (iv) new  social security services to
indicate source of financing.
*  Debt/revenue ratios are subject to limits to be established by the Senate. A draft Senate
resolution on net federal debt establishes a maximum net debt/revenue ratio of 3.5. The ratio
is presently 3.45. The draft resolution of sub-national debt establishes a maximum net
debt/revenue ratio of 2.0 for states and of 1.2 for municipalities. As many states and
municipalities exceed these ratios, a linear adjustment during a fifteen year period is
contemplated. Excess debt needs to be corrected in 12 months.
*  Borrowing is subject to: (i) textual legal authorization to borrow and inclusion in budget; (ii)
compliance with limits on the debt stock; (iii) total borrowing not to exceed investment
expenditures; (iv) Senate authorization (for external loans); and (v) compliance with LFR;
* Intergovernmental lending is prohibited except by public financial institutions. Guarantees
are permitted, provided that a counter-guarantee with a higher value is furnished and that the
borrower is not in default with the guarantor;
*  Disclosure and dissemination of PPAs, Budget Directive Laws (LDOs), Budgets, Public
Accounts, public debt, budget execution summary reports, and Fiscal Management Reports is
mandatory;
*  The federal government is responsible for consolidation of public sector accounts and
establishment of a federal registry of public sector debt.
8.     With the LFR, Brazil has then combined two key fiscal institutions: ex-ante constraints
and multi-annual planning, i.e., the three-year fiscal objectives that must be indicated in the laws
that regulate budget programming. It has also strengthened numerical limits, or the debt/revenue
ceilings that the Senate must issue. These new features add to the dominance of the Finance
Ministry in preparing the budget and to multi-annual planning (the PPA). Thus Brazil now has
institutions in place that allow aggregate fiscal discipline.
9.     As indicated before, the effectiveness of budget institutions depend on a number of
factors (para. 5). In the case of Brazil, effectiveness shortcomings include:
3 The distributed percentages for the federal legislative, judiciary, executive, and ministerio publico (Attorney
General's Office) respectively are 2.5%, 6%, 40.9%, and 0.6% for the federal level; and 3%, 6%, 49%, and 2% for
the state level. In municipalities, the personnel revenue ratio cannot exceed 54% and the other branches together
cannot exceed 6%.



70
*  Excessive autonomy of some parts of the budget: autonomy has been tempered by legislation
that "taxes" autonomous expenditures to increase flexibility);
*  Lack of comprehensiveness of the budget (due to the impact of sub-national budgets, over
which the federal governrment has no control); the adverse impact of this lack of
comprehensiveness, which emerges out of Brazil's federalized system, has been tempered by
stronger budget constraints faced by sub-national governments due to debt-refinancing
agreements that securitized debt repayment obligations and stronger legal constraints on debt
and borrowing;
*  Weakness of ex post restraints, as a result of excessive supplementary budgets: monetary
stability and stricter rules has reduced the need for supplementary budgets;
*  Relative softness of budget constraints on sub-national governments: as discussed, budget
constraints on sub-national governments are now stronger due to securitization of their debt
repayment obligations and stronger constraints on debt and borrowing (partly established
through the LFR);
*  Inadequate information with regard to fiscal performance, particularly at the sub-national
level: the LFR has addressed this issue by mandating extensive disclosure and dissemination
of budget documents, reports and accounts.
*  Limited ex-post reconciliation: with the Law of Fiscal Responsibility, reconciliation of
outcomes with plans is mandated, through Fiscal Management Reports, issued every four
months by all governments.
10.   Incentives for compliance with the LFR come from Brazil's macroeconomic policy
framework, from the LFR itself, from penal provisions, and from the stronger budget constraint
faced by sub-national governments. First, political support for Brazil's stable macroeconomic
framework places a constraint on monetary financing of the federal deficit. Brazil now has an
inflation targeting framework in place that reflects country commitment to monetary stability.
Targets were set at 8%, 6% and 4% respectively for the IPCA index duringl999-2001, with a
margin on each side of two percentage points. Inflation in 1999 was 8.9%. In its September
2000 inflation report, BCB expected an inflation of 6.7% for the year 2000 (similar to the
market's median expectation in September of 6.3% for the year) and an inflation below 4% for
2001 (somewhat lower than the market's median expectation in September of 4.3% for 2001).
Furthermore, the high level of real interest rates in Brazil places a constraint on excessive resort
to public sector borrowing. With interest rates an irnportant determinant of growth, federal
policies, including fiscal policies, have an incentive to reduce public sector indebtedness, not to
increase it.
11.   Second, the LFR has five sources of remedies for various instances of non compliance
with the LFR. These are prohibition of intergovernmental voluntary transfers (excluding
transfers for health, education, and social assistance), borrowing, guarantees, constitutional
transfers, and adjustment of primary balances. One or more of these remedies apply to non-
compliance with several provisions regarding tax collection, personnel expenditure limits, debt
limits, default, and fiscal accounts and reports. Because transfers for health, education, and
social assistance are excluded from the voluntary transfers remedy and borrowing is a minor
share of revenues in most governments, particularly municipal, the effectiveness of LFR
remedies is limited. Nevertheless, in many governments, access to the included transfers is



71
important and the remedy may be a factor in encouraging compliance. For example, many
municipalities are reportedly making efforts to raise collection of their property taxes, partly to
avoid the LFR provision that prohibits voluntary transfers to those governments that do not
collect projected taxes.38
12.   Third, penal provisions have been added to strengthen compliance. The new Law of
Fiscal Crimes (Law No. 10.028 of October 19, 2000), added non-compliance with certain LFR
provisions to Brazil's Penal Code (Decree-Law 2848 of 1940), to Law 1079 of 1950 (covering
misconduct by federal and state authorities, including the president, the attomey general
(procurador geral), ministers, governors, and state secretaries), and to Decree-Law 201 of 1967
(covering misconduct of municipal elected officials). As a result, under the Penal Code officials
that borrow illegally, that include uncommitted expenditures or expenditures exceeding limits in
accounts payable (restos a pagar ), that instruct payment of non-authorized expenditures, that
grant guarantees without required counter-guarantees, that fail to clear amounts exceeding legal
limits in accounts payable, that raise personnel expenditures during the last year in office of an
administration, or that issue unauthorized public debt bonds, are now subject to imprisonment.
13.   Under Law 1079, officials (president, ministers, governors, and state secretaries) that do
not instruct the reduction of debt to legal limits, that instruct or authorize expenditures not
included in the budget, that fail to repay/cancel loans made exceeding limits, that fail to repay
advanced revenue loans (Antecipa,do de Receita Or,amentaria) within the year, that instruct or
authorize illegal intergovernmental lending, that borrow against un-accrued future tax receipts,
that use the proceeds of bond issues for a different destination than that for which they were
intended, or that extended or received voluntary transfers in conflict with legal provisions, are
now to be fired. Under Decree-Law 201, the same applies to municipal elected officials.
14.   Also, under the new Law of Fiscal Crimes, officials that fail to disseminate the Fiscal
Management Report, to send LDO proposals without the Annex of Fiscal Targets, to reduce
expenditure commitments and payments (movimenta,dofinanceira) when required by law, or to
implement measures to reduce personnel expenditures to legal limits, are subject to a personal
fine of 30% of their annual salaries.
15.   Fourth, compliance with the LFR is also encouraged by the stricter budget constraint
being faced by sub-national governments. This stricter constraint originates in (i) the debt
refinancing agreements with most states and some municipalities, whereby the federal
government granted refinancing at a low interest rate and a capped debt service/revenue ratio,
with the condition of securitizing debt service payments with constitutional and voluntary
transfers; (ii) the more restricted access to borrowing emanating from the prohibition of
intergovernmental lending and more stringent conditions imposed on new borrowing.
Possible Impact/Benefits of the LFR
16.   In addition to the LFR, there are other reforms that are having an impact on Brazil's
aggregate fiscal performance, defined as the path of the primary balance, the public sector
borrowing requirement, and the stock of debt. These reforms include the Government's 1998
Fiscal Stability Plan, which runs through 2001 and contemplates measures to generate fiscal
3 See Gazeta Mercantil, December 5, 2000, P. A-8.



72
surpluses that suffice to reduce the public sectors debt/revenue ratio; the refinancing agreements
with most states and some municipalities, which strengthened the budget constraints faced by
sub-national governments; and social security and administrative reforms, which are helping
contain personnel expenditures.
17.   The impact of these reforms can be described as allowing the fiscal stance indicated by
the Federal Government in its last Budget Guidelines Law (Lei de Diretrizes Orqamentarias,
LDO). In the Annex on Fiscal Targets to that Law, the federal primary balance is targeted at
2.6% of GDP in 2001, 2.2% in 2002, and 1.8% in 2003. The fiscal stance for the overall public
sector would then be equivalent to 3% of GDP in 2001 (the target under the revised Fiscal
Stability Program), and 2.7% in 2002 and 2.2% in 2003, assuming a constant primary balance of
states and municipalities. The impacts are discriminated as follows:
*  The Government's 1998 Fiscal Stability Plan provides the basic framework of fiscal
policies for 1999-01 and the fiscal targets to be attained. It provides an ex-ante agreement
and a commitment to fiscal stability. Since the Fiscal Stability Plan has been in force since
1998, it provides a positive test of the possible working of the LFR.
*  The LFR provides the institutionalized Fiscal Stability framework for fiscal policies at all
government levels, including provisions on fiscal targets, revenues, expenditures, debt,
borrowing, and transparency described above. These strengthen fiscal planning, budget
execution, and budget constraints. It is already providing this framework at the federal level
for 2001, as the federal 2001 was issued in July 2000, following approval of the LFR the
previous month.
*  The debt refinancing agreements with most states and some municipalities strengthen the
budget constraints face by these governments through (i) a securitization of debt service
obligations which is forcing fiscal adjustment at the sub-national level ; (ii) a commitment to
a set of fiscal targets (gross debt/revenue ratio, primary balance, personnel expenditures,
revenues, privatizationlconcessions, investment expenditures.
*  Under the Administrative Reform approved in 1998, governments will be able to dismiss
personnel when their personnel expenditures exceed limits regime (full regulation of this
provision still needs to be completed). Furthermore, the public sector will hire through the
private sector labor regime, under which retirement benefits are much lower (1.8 minimum
salaries) than under the public sector regime (13 minimum salaries, on the average). These
reforms will have an impact only in the very long term.
*  Social security reforms, which have increased contribution time, reduced retirement time,
reduced pension benefits, or increased contributions. These have temporarily stabilized the
social security deficit.
In sum, the actions with a significant effect now are the 1998 Fiscal Stability Plan Stability (an
ex-ante agreement on fiscal targets), the LFR (the institutionalization and deepening of ex-ante
constraints on fiscal targets and ex-post reconciliation of those targets), the refinancing
agreements, and the recent social security reforms. The overall fiscal impact can be described by
the expected path of the ratio of the public sector's net debt to GDP. The impact thus far has
been to stabilize the debt level within 48%-50% of GDP after having risen sharply between 1995
(30.3%) and January 1999 (53.4%). This level is likely to decline slowly after 2002.



73
18.   One of the critical challenges of fiscal adjustment is fiscal adjustment at the sub-national
level. As indicated, the debt refinancing agreements both aim at deepening adjustment.
Ultimately, the joint effects of the LFR and the other provisions discussed above can be
summarized in the behavior of the public sector debt, where changes reflect the behavior of the
primary balance and the interest rate. Chart 1 shows the ratio of net debt to disposable revenues
on a monthly basis for the federal and sub-national govermnents since January 1998. 39 The ratio
of net federal debt to net federal revenues increased from 1.2 in December 1997 to about two
(i.e., debt twice as much as revenues) in January 1999 (when the dollar denominated debt
climbed as a result of floating the exchange rate that month). The ratio of net sub-national debt
to net sub-national revenues increased from 1.5 in December 1997 to 1.8 in August, 1999. Then,
as a result of the 1998 federal Fiscal Stability Plan (which was strengthened following the early
1999 devaluation), the debt refinancing agreements, and other provisions limiting sub-national
access to borrowing, debt/revenue trends changed course, with some decline in the federal
debt/revenue ratio from the high point in mid-1999 and a stabilization of the subnational
debt/revenue ratio within 1.7-1.8 after August 1999. The LFR is expected to reinforce this
change of course as it enters into full operation after approval in May 1999. For example, in the
Annex of Fiscal Targets to the LDO for the 2001 budget, the federal government aims at
reducing the ratio of federal debt
