One critical factor here is the
strength of budget constraints faced by the public sector. A relaxed budget constraint, in terms
of a relaxed access to credit, would weaken the relevance of the LFR, as governments would
plan on expanding expenditures with additional borrowing, leading to increased indebtedness.
The risk of relaxing budget constraints is contained by Brazil's commitment to low inflation and
39 Debt ceilings under the LFR are to be expressed as ratios to net revenues rather than as ratios to GDP (Para. 3 of
LFR Article 30).



74
by current levels of debt that are already high by historical standards. Brazil's commitment to
low inflation means that it would bot be politically rewarding to risk fiscal instability resulting in
monetary expansion. High levels of debt mean that access to new debt is costly and that service
on existing debt is already a heavy burden on public budgets. Higher indebtedness would further
increase cost or reduce access, and further worsen the burden of debt service on public budgets.
Both these factors (commitment to low inflation and high debt levels) suggest that the budget
constraint faced by Brazil's government is likely to be stronger than in the past.
20.   A second critical factor is weak enforcement of the LFR. Weak enforcement may result
due to (i) the exclusion of voluntary transfers for health and education from the prohibition to
provide voluntary transfers to those governments that do not comply with key LFR provisions to
with an adverse effect on fiscal planning or fiscal execution; (ii) the low share of new credit in
the revenues of many governnents (new credit is another remedy for non-compliance with key
LFR provisions; and (iii) inadequate monitoring/prosecution of non-compliance with LFR
provisions with penal implications under the Law of Fiscal Crimes. The exclusion referred to in
(i) above indeed means that the voluntary transfers remedy will not be a critical factor
determining the success of the LFR (although, as discussed before, some governments are
reacting positively to the possibility of its application). Similarly, the ban of credit will be
irrelevant to the many governments that borrow little. Nevertheless, for some governments that
are envisaging new credit operations to finance critical investment projects, the credit remedies
likely to encourage compliance with the LFR. Finally, on (iii) above, there is the perceptions that
penal legislation is an important deterrent to official misconduct, and that the strength of such a
deterrent has been increasing. Indeed, recent data on dismissals by reason of misconduct have
shown a significant increase over the last few years. It is believed that such a rise responds more
to better monitoring and prosecution than to a higher propensity for misconduct.



75
ANNEX 5: THE PPA 2000-2003 AND MODERNIZATION OF BRAZIL'S PUBLIC ADMINISTRATION
THE HISTORICAL DEVELOPMENT OF THE FEDERAL ADMINISTRATION
1.    The basis for a modernized public administration was laid in the 1930s as the Vargas
regime conferred a new development role on the state. Systems for a meritocratic civil service,
public procurement, and budget control were established. This investment no doubt created a
level of administrative competence and effectiveness which may have distinguished Brazil from
many of its neighbors. But from the start, the rules emphasized a rigid control of processes, and
there has been a more or less permanent effort to further reform the administrative process.
Success in this has been limited, until recently at least. In response to a perception that increasing
patronage and clientelism were undermining the quality of the administration, the 1988
Constitution went in the opposite direction and reinforced the inflexibility of the system by
giving job stability to public servants at all levels of government and severely limiting the power
of the Executive to restructure the administrative apparatus and introduce performance-oriented
incentives system.
2.    The 1995-99 reforms. The early 1990s were, as part of a wave of "first-generation'
reforms, a period of frustrated downsizing. Civil servants were substantially successful in
resisting the efforts of the Collor Government to remove a large number of them. The
Government also severely reduced the number of ministries, only to have the next Government
(of Itamar Franco) reverse this. Meanwhile, administrative capacity had substantially weakened
as a result of the economic crisis that began in the 1980s.
3.    Administrative modernization came back on to the agenda in 1995, with the creation of
the Ministry for Federal Administration and Reform of the State (MARE), under the first
Cardoso Government. MARE developed an ambitious approach to putting the house back in
order, enshrined in its "Plan Director". The Government achieved important constitutional
reforms to reverse some of the inflexibilities of the 1988 Constitution. It also did much to re-
establish discipline and merit in the civil service. This included cleaning up the federal payroll,
as well as re-establishing an effective senior executive service through a Commission, DAS. The
DAS system incorporates both senior career officials and political appointments into a limited
number of posts, with a uniform structure of remuneration and appropriate qualification
requirements. DAS thereby creates an effective corps of senior officials, as well as provides for
transparent and meritocratic rules for political appointments. On another front, the Government
made some notable advances in transparency through various information technology initiatives.
4.    But MARE made less progress in its most ambitious objective, This was to move from a
"bureaucratic" to a "managerial" administration, principally by radically altering the structure of
the federal executive. The strategy took its cue from the leading reforms then going on in some
OECD countries, but the design of the reform was substantially adapted to the Brazilian
situation. New organizational entities would be created to hive off large amounts of government
activity: "Executive Agencies" would be a key service arm of the government, enjoying
considerable managerial autonomy and linked to ministries through performance contracts;
"Social Organizations" would be created under private law to provide contestable services of a
public nature with partial public subsidy. In the event, few such new entities have been created,



76
partly because the government was not prepared to provide priority in the flow of budget funds
to such agencies. But it may also be the case that changing the management culture through
changing the organizations was too frontal an approach to change, hence too threatening to
existing interests in the bureaucracy. Organizational change of the type originally envisaged now
appears to be stillborn.
5.    The state of the federal public administration todav. While it did not move as far as it
had hoped towards creating a results-oriented culture, the government's reform efforts of 1995-
99 did succeed in a recuperation of the effectiveness of the public administration (as well as of
public financial administration), while they also succeeded in putting further performance-based
managerial reform firmly on the agenda. We can venture the following hypotheses about the
current (pre-PPA) state of administrative performance:
*  Brazil's administration is, compared to many of its neighbors, reasonably well endowed with
middle- and higher-level professionals, thanks to the DAS system and thanks to ministry-by-
ministry merit-based career systems and reasonable pay levels. In addition, informal
networks may serve to reinforce the effectiveness of the higher cadres. Yet numerous
imperfections remain in career rules and salary systems. For instance, horizontal (inter-
ministry) and vertical (promotion) mobility are impeded; the competitiveness of salaries with
the private sector has been eroded since the mid-1990s; pay scales are compressed. One
result of these imperfections is to accentuate the unevenness of levels of capability and
professionalism across ministries.
*  The improvement in fiscal stability since the Real Plan has allowed a recovery in the budget
and financial management system as an instrument of managerial control.
  With these reasonable levels of human resources and financial control, Brazil's federal
ministries are effective, relative to their homologues in many other countries of the region.
For better or worse, the ministries are marked by different cultures, perhaps reflecting their
different objectives and challenges, different institutional histories, and the often distinct
characteristics of their professional corps.
-  It is not clear how Brazil's political system affect the capacity of civil servants and ministries
to work without undue particularistic pressures. Fragmented parties, coalition government,
and the strong constitutional role of Congress and State Governors might all be elements
expected to add to these pressures. There is evidence, in academic studies and observations
among analysts, of strong political pressure affecting financial resource allocations. Yet a
first impression is that Brazil's administration does not face the same level of day-to-day
politicization that some other countries in the region experience.
*  In spite of the overall capacity of the administration, in a comparative-regional context at
least, its financial and other procedures, ministerial structures, and working cultures have
been designed (prior to the PPA at least) to concentrate on form rather than results. This is
reflected in almost seven decades of effective application of strongly hierarchical rules and
the persistent failure of reform efforts to change that paradigm. Effective hierarchy has
probably served Brazil better than the ineffective systems - ineffective because they have
been undermined by patronage and clientelism-- typifying many countries of the region. But
there now appears to be a strong consensus in the leading parts of the government (and
consistent with the viewpoint of MARE) that it is time to transform a bureaucracy organized
along Weberian lines into a more managerial format.



77
6.    The approach of the PPA 2000-2003 to administrative modernization. The PPA's new
approach to administrative modernization departs from similar managerialist objectives to
MARE's Plan Director. But the PPA adopts different tactics, seeking to reorganize the way
government business is done around clearly defined programs, rather than frontally re-structuring
organizations per se. It can be inferred that the PPA's implicit intent is to challenge the
organization of existing agencies by putting the programs inside them. The main building blocks
of PPA's approach to management are as follows:
*  The government's business is organized into programs which stress the desired output,
rather than the logic of production. In the PPA preparation process (1998-99) the Planning
and Budget Secretariats of the Planning Ministry effectively worked in parallel to re-
apportion all of the federal government's business into 365 programs. (In passing the PPA
the Congress added 23 Programs to bring the total to 388.) Each Program is attached to one
federal Ministry or agency, although many of these Programs will require actions in other
ministries or at sub-national levels of government. In fact, these Programs can be seen as
essentially putting existing public business into new boxes, while adding some new business
(i.e., akin to incremental budgeting). For tactical reasons there was relatively little emphasis
on cutting existing business. But the new boxes, as well as some of the newer Programs,
emphasize a strategic approach that emphasizes outputs and outcomes rather than inputs or
processes. For instance, a transport corridor Program would emphasize the integrated multi-
modal system that is needed to move goods or people from A to B, in contrast to a program
to build, say, a road. Thus, in order to provide a more effective approach to satisfying the
populace's real demands, these Programs imply a challenge to existing government
"production" processes and the organizations they fall into.
*  Programs provide a transparent basis for performance orientation. Programs have simple,
self-explanatory titles, objectives, subsidiary actions necessary to obtain these objectives, and
output indicators for these actions. This information is publicly available through the
Internet. In turn, Programs and actions are clearly linked to required budgetary resources for
the four-year PPA period.
*  The Program-based PPA is fully linked to the budget document. The PPA combines current
and investment costs of programs. The 2000 Budget has adopted the same program basis as
the PPA, and the first year of the PPA has been fully translated into the 2000 Budget
document. It remains to be seen, however, how the PPA and the annual budgets adjust
themselves to each other over time as the budget execution diverges from the approved
budget and thus from the PPA. There is also a question of actual fund allocations to
Programs vs. organizational units. Except for those ministries such as Environment, which
have adjusted their organizational structures to the Program structure, there may still be an
effective disconnect between actual flow of funds ( to the traditional organizational units)
and the PPA allocations (to Programs). These points would still need to be clarified in
subsequent work.
*  The four-year PPA has procedural links with three-year macro planning, but how the
relationship will work in practice and how the PPA can adapt to unexpected shocks is not yet
clear. Annual changes in the budgetary resource envelope will be guided by the macro-
targeting of the Law of Fiscal Responsibility (LRF). Normal year-on-year incremental



78
adjustments to the Programs will occur through various Program amendments that will
require administrative decisions and, in some cases, legal amendments to the PPA. The
Planning Ministry has identified 87 Strategic Programs on the basis of a system of weighted
criteria. But how this might be formalized as a guide to managing annual adjustments in PPA
and the budget is not yet clear. Nor is it clear how the PPA would be adjusted in the event of
an unexpected shock.
*  The PPA system is strongly committed to an evaluation system, but this has not yet been fully
developed. The Planning Ministry intends to carry out the first round of plan and program
evaluations in partnership with the Institute of Applied Economic Research (IPEA). Further
work on the evaluation framework will be undertaken in 2001, probably with Bank
cooperation under the TA loan currently under preparation.
* The Programs and their links with budget and expenditure management are supported by a
series of Internet-based information systems. A management information system (SIG)
provides information and feedback on Programs and their implementation to Program
Managers, SPI, and Ministries, and is being extended to the public. Brazil is also well served
by a series of related systems for budgeting and execution (SIAFI, SIDOR?).
-  Managers are appointed for each Program. Working within the structure of a Ministry or
agency, they have the responsibility for executing that Program, although in most cases this
responsibility has not (yet) been matched with the necessary resources. Managers are
appointed by the Ministry or agency within which the Program falls. They are usually drawn
from existing senior staff and, typically, continue to hold other line responsibilities (such as
Director). The conditions under which the Managers work vary across Ministries and
agencies. In some cases, Programs have been incorporated within existing organizational
charts, somewhat as if they were departments or divisions. In other cases, Managers find
themselves as change agents, with few or no resources and with the task of using their access
to information and moral authority to get other parts of the ministry or other federal or sub-
national agencies to cooperate. In either case, to be effective Managers often have to work
across formal structures and through informal channels - across ministries, with sub-national
governments, and so on. This often reflects the "matrix" natures of Programs which are
intended to produce outputs through coordinated actions among relevant sectors or sub-
sectors (such as a transport corridor) rather than project outputs within a particular sector or
sub-sector (such as a road). Thus the Programn approach, often at odds with existing
organizational structures, is implicitly designed to apply pressure to change those structures.
Change is already emerging in some Ministries, such as Environment and Transport.
*  The Program approach and the role of the Manager are being strongly supported by the
training activities of the National Schoolfor Public Administration (ENAP), as well as by the
Planning Ministry itself
7.    The implicit political approach of the PPA to managerial reform can be distinguished
from that of the Plan Director. Both have sought similar performance-oriented objectives, but the
PPA has had a less frontal approach, planting the seeds of change through the Program approach,
but establishing in the first place only transparency and strategic clarity, and not yet pushing on
full accountability and the incentives necessary for this. The pace is not being forced:
organizations are being challenged, but not directly changed.



79
SOME HYPOTHESES ABOUT THE IMPACT OF PPA
8.    The approach of the PPA has had an initial impact which can be characterized as laying
the basis for further improvement in three dimensions of public expenditure performance:
* Macroeconomic balance: a clear link between planning and budgeting processes has been
established. While the macroeconomic framework for the PPA was apparently based on
conservative projections, the PPA is not itself the macroeconomic instrument. This is the role
of the LRF and the annual budget cycle. It remains to be seen how well the PPA will be
articulated with the LRF and the annual cycle.
* Prioritization: the PPA so far has, by establishing Programs, clarified -- i.e. made transparent
-- the Government's plans and projected these over a four-year period. In general, the
Government has not so far used the PPA process to change its priorities, though it has
identified a strategic core among its existing programs. A better basis for subsequent change
has now been established. For instance, the room for rationalizing - reducing waste -will
now become clearer.
* Efficiency issues have been addressed in two directions. First, Managers have been given
some responsibility for promoting Programs and achieving their goals, though the steps taken
so far have been modest. Second, by their design, many Programs have adopted a more
strategic approach emphasizing end-needs of citizens, rather than processes.
9.    Finally, the PPA seems to have a strong political grounding. The implicit tactic is to first
seek transparency, better public-expenditure practices, and more assured resources before
rationalizing Programs. It is hoped that this will thereby minimize the threat to bureaucrats. The
reform is substantially "home grown", using lessons from the Plan Director and the previous
PPA (Brasil am Aqao). And it seems to be taking political root: it has the support of the President
and the leading ministries, as well as of a number of senior managers.
THE ISSUES TO BE ADDRESSED.
10.   The challenge Brazil has set itself of moving its bureaucratic mode towards greater
performance orientation is formidable. Among the non-OECD countries, few can be said to have
made any serious progress beyond Chile, Malaysia, and Singapore. In spite of the much
discussed (and sometimes disputed) achievements of countries such as New Zealand and the
United Kingdom, the New Public Management is still in many ways terra incognita. It is clear
that, given the nature of public goods and services, the public sector cannot adopt all the methods
of the private sector. It is also likely that for countries such as Brazil, managerial reform can only
go as far and as fast as politics and popular demand will allow it.
11.   Brazil's greatest challenge in preserving the PPA experiment will be to maintain fiscal
stability. If Programs do not have a credible assurance of available budgetary resources over the
medium term, performance is bound to fall short. Given that Brazil still has not completed the
process of fiscal reform and given the volatility of international capital markets, fiscal stability
over the long term is far from assured, and fiscal shocks must be anticipated. The PPA and
budgetary authorities need to ensure that the links of the plan and the budget are improved and
that an agreed procedure exists for accommodating the PPA to unforeseen shocks.



80
12.   The process of managerial reform is only just beginning. The introduction of the Program
and the concept of the Manager have laid some building blocks for this, but the challenge will be
to give Managers enough resources and authority to make them accountable. This in turn will
require organizational change, reinforcement of human resources, and the introduction of
monitoring and evaluation as a regular activity. The way ahead is not obvious, there is room for
experiment, and, for the moment at least, there is virtue in heterogeneity of forms and
approaches. It would make sense for SPI to encourage different approaches in different
ministries and invest in understanding these differences. In this regard, it could be useful to
create a taxonomy of different types of Program according to the "production" problems they
tackle (e.g. who produces the final "product"-the federal government or, say a municipality?
How measurable is the output? In what sense is an output strategic?). As managerial reform
develops, Brazil will in turn need to adjust the present model of budgeting and accounting for the
Programs. Full managerial accountability will, for instance, require full costing of Programs.
13.   There will be a constant challenge of matching the timing of progress in the PPA to
political realities, in the form both of "big-picture" politics - for instance "pork-barrel" behavior
- and of bureaucratic politics - the resistance of civil servants to change. It is such considerations
which will indicate when and how fast ineffective or politically-inspired Programs can be cut.



81
ANNEX 6: BRAZIL'S INTEGRATED FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT SYSTEM
INTRODUCTION
1.   In 1986 the Brazilian government initiated the development of an integrated
financial management system (IFMS), with the purpose of improving its control over
public expenditure. Known as SIAFI, the current system became operative in January
1987. It is a very solid and proven system managed by the national treasury (STN), which
is part of the Ministry of Finance (MOF).  The system is currently  processing
approximately 50,000 documents per day originating in more than 4,500 government units.
SIAFI provides on-line access to over 33,000 individual users. In brief, SIAFI is the core
system used by the Brazilian government to program, process and control the financial
execution of the federal budget. It also is the federal government's main accounting and
fiscal reporting system.
2.    Notwithstanding that over its 13 years in operation SIAFI has undergone a number
of functional modifications and upgradings the system is close to become obsolete because
of new technological developments and major changes in Brazilian fiscal rules, and new
approaches to fiscal management with important effects on institutional arrangements.
Maintenance of the system, both functionally and technologically is becoming increasingly
costly, making upgradings and operational integration with other modem government
systems more difficult..
3.    The introduction and implementation by the federal government of (a) a program-
based multiannual plan budgeting framework (PPA), (b) a Fiscal Responsibility Law
(LRF), (c) improved institutional arrangement for public debt management, and (d) new
institutional arrangements for asset/liability management, impose additional fiscal
monitoring and evaluation challenges that cannot be efficiently undertaken by SIAFI unless
the system undergoes major functional and technological upgrading. Taxation reforms
presently on the drawing board may also require important changes in SIAFI's
functionality, in particular in relation to managing the distribution of revenues to states and
municipalities. Consequently, since 1999 the STN has been pursuing a project to develop a
so-called SIAFI 21st Century proposal with the objective of accommodating SIAFI to this
new fiscal management environment and modernizing its technological platform.
4.    Originally, the development of the new SIAFI was to begin in 2000, but scheduling
and budget constraints forced a one-year postponement of the program. The STN reports
that funding of the program for an approximate amount of US $ 20 million has been
included in the federal budget proposal for 2001 presently being considered by the
Brazilian Congress. Additional federal funding amounting to approximately US$ 29
million in 2002, and US$ 1.5 million in 2003 will be required to complete the deployment
of the new system. This includes the development of a new multi-modular IFMS software
package, significant upgrading of the hardware and communication platforms, and massive
training of users. Under present plans, the new SIAFI would become operational January
2003, completely replacing the current SIAFI.



82
OVERVIEW OF THE BRAZILL4NBUDGETING PROCESS
5.    Though it is not an specific purpose of this Annex to discuss the Brazilian budgeting
process, but to review the SIAFI 21" Century proposal, it is useful to provide a brief
overview of such a process since it is the operating framework of SIAFI.
6.    Financial management and audit systems. The Brazilian government has recently
redefined the organization of its federal planning, budgeting, financial administration,
accounting and internal control systems by way of a Presidential decree (Medida
Provisoria Nro. 2.036-80 of June 27, 2000), which has the force of law. Four distinct
federal systems have been defined:
(a) The Federal Planning and Budget Systems, under the responsibility of the Ministry
of Planning and Budget (MP), with the mission of (i) formulating strategic planning at
the national level; (ii) formulating the social and economic development plans at the
national, sectorial and regional level; (iii) formulating the multi-annual plan (PPA), and
annual budget guidelines (LDO), as well as the annual federal budgets (OGU); (iv)
managing the federal planning and budgeting processes; and, (v) promoting co-
ordination with local governments, seeking compatibility in the norms and actions of
the various systems at the federal, estate, district and municipal levels. The decree also
lists the various specific activities to be developed by the central, sectorial and specific
planning and budgeting units.
(b) The Federal Financial Administration System, under the responsibility of the STN,
with the mission of (i) balancing the national treasury, managing the national treasury's
assets and liabilities; (ii) preparing the financial programming of the national treasury,
managing its unified account (Conta Unica); (iii) formulating financing policies for
public expenditure; (iv) managing internal and external public debt under the Union's
or the National Treasury's responsibility, including that with international agencies; (v)
issuing financial programming, budget and financial execution standards; (vi)
promoting the monitoring, systematization and recording of the execution of public
expenditure; and, (vii) promoting co-ordination with the other constitutional powers and
government sectors in matters dealing with financial programming.
(c) Federal Accounting System, also under the responsibility of the STN, with the mission
of (i) maintaining the accounting systems the Union's budget, financial and patrimonial
administration; (ii) keeping record of the operations of governmental organs and entities
and their effects on the structure of the Union's patrimony; (iii) keeping record of
outstanding revenues, of the execution of budget appropriations, as modified by
additional credits (i.e., budget modifications during the fiscal year), of estimated and
collected revenues, expenditure commitments, accruals and payments against such
revenues, and available balances; (iv) keeping records on the operations and balances of
anyone responsible for collecting revenues, ordering and making expenditures, or
administering en entrusted assets; (v) keeping record of the patrimonial situation of
public entities and variations thereon; (vi) keeping records of the cost of federal
administration's programs and units; (vii) keeping records of the application of the
Union's resources by federative unit; and (viii) keeping record of waivers of revenues
by federal organs and entities. The decree also lists specific responsibilities of the
accounting units under the system; and



83
(d) The Federal Internal Control System, under the responsibility of the Federal Control
Secretariat (FCS) of the MOF, with the mission of (i) evaluating the compliance of the
targets of the multi-annual plan (PPA); (ii) fiscalizing and evaluating the execution of
the government's programs, including decentralized actions funded with resources of
the Union's budgets, and considering the level of execution of established target and
objectives and the quality of management performance; (iii) evaluating of the execution
of the Union's budgets; (iv) controlling credit operations, including guarantees, and of
the Union's rights and assets; (iv) providing information about the physical and
financial execution of projects and of permanent activities funded through the Union's
budgets; (v) performing audits of the management of federal resources under the
responsibility of public or private organs and entities; (vi) investigating and evaluating
acts or facts deemed illegal or irregular performed by public or private agents involving
the use of federal resources, and take them as may warranted before the responsible
accounting unit for further action; (vii) performing audits of the accounting, financial,
budget and human resources systems, and all other systems; (viii) evaluating the
performance of internal audit activities in the indirect federal administration; (ix)
preparing the annual report on fiscal accounts submitted by the president to Congress;
and, (x) creating conditions for the performance of social or citizen controls over the
programs funded by the Union's budgets.
While these systems already existed in substantially comparable forms before the
enactment of the decree, the importance of these renewed definitions is their updating and
upgrading in terns of PPA and the LRF objectives, replacing standards dating as far back
as 1983, and supporting new institutional arrangements.
7.    Institutional arrangements of the Brazilian budgetin2! process Budgeting in
Brazil is organized into two distinct processes. The MP is responsible for the formulation
of the annual federal budget proposal (OGU, for General Budget of the Union) and of
programming its execution once it is approved by Congress, whereas the MOF is
responsible for the control and accounting of budget execution, and financial programming
thereon. The Brazilian annual budget formulation process is regulated by three main legal
instruments, as indicated in Table A6. 1.

8.    Once the annual budget law is approved by Congress, the MP and the MOF interact
with each other and with spending units, initiating a continuous flow of decision-making,
evaluation and information processes to manage, control and assess the physical and
financial performance of the budget during the fiscal year, as illustrated in Box A6. 1.

9.   IT systems supportin2 the budget process. The MP's  planning, budget
formulation and budget programming functions are supported by a system known as
SIDOR, while MOF budget execution, financial planning and accounting functions are
supported by SIAFI. While not integrated as a single operating system, SIDOR and SIAFI
exchange data in the course of their daily operation. To accommodate program-based
multiannual planning (PPA) the MP introduced in September 1999 a new system known as
SIG, which draws on information processed by SIDOR and SIAFI to enable program
managers to monitor and evaluate program execution and performance. While SIAFI
provides historical and current information contributing to the formulation of the annual
federal budget proposal, the actual formulation process under the purview of the MP is
supported by SIDOR. In the preparation of the annual budget proposal, spending units,
ministries and other sectorial agencies interact with the MP using SIDOR's budget
formulation facilities.
10.   Once the annual federal budget law (OGU) is approved by Congress and
promulgated by the Executive Branch, the MP proceeds to program the execution of the
budget on the basis of the authorized appropriations or credits. Budget programming by
spending unit is formulated using the MP's SIDOR system from which it is transferred by
magnetic media to SIAFI to be used by the STN for the financial programming of budget
execution. Federal government cash resources are held at the treasury's unified account at
the Central Bank, which concentrates all revenues and from which all payments are made
using Banco do Brazil as the treasury's appointed financial agent.  During budget
execution, SIAFI makes automatic accounting entries for all budget and financial
transactions, and produces the financial statements of the federal government, as well as the
consolidated financial statements of the Union which consolidate the financial situation of
the federal, state and municipal governments and other relevant decentralized entities.
Throughout the fiscal year the MP's SIDOR and SIG systems will extract data from SIAFI
to monitor and control budget programming compliance by spending units, and to evaluate
program performance and results under the PPA. Also, during the year, the MP will
process modifications to the budget approved by Congress (transfers between
appropriations and additional credits of various types, some of which require Congress
approval) and through its SIDOR system the MP will export to SIAFI the resulting
variations in available credits, updating budget appropriations balances.
DESCRIPTIONAAND ASSESSMENT OF THE CURRENT SL4FI
11.  In order to understand and assess the scope of the proposed SIAFI 21st Century
project, it is important to outline the operating indicators, the financial management
functionality, and the technological platform of the current SIAFI system.
12.   SIAFI - Operating Indicators.    SIAFI has a production version  (SIAFI
Operational) used by spending units, and a management version (SIAFI Gerencial) used
mainly by management units. The current operating indicators of the present SIAFI, are
summarized in Table A.6.2.



87
TABLE A6.2 - OPERATING INDICATORS OF SIAFI
CURRENT                    SIAFI         SIAFI
OPERATING INDICATORS             Operacional    Gerencial     TOTAL
Registered users                           33,458          1,787       35,245
Average user log-ons per day               74,000           308        74,308
Simultaneous users installed capacity       2,382           482         2,864

13.   SIAFI is used by all ministries agencies of the executive, legislative and judiciary
branches and other entities financed by the federal budget, as the main tool for registering,
monitoring and controlling their respective budget and financial execution transactions.
The system automatically posts the corresponding accounting entries. In the course of
operations, SIAFI is also used as a management information system and as a source of
information for internal and external audits the system is managed by the STN, who
establishes SIAFI's operating logic and standards, and provides support to spending units
using the system. the STN is in turn supported by SERPRO, a decentralized data processing
services unit of the finance ministry, who is responsible for the technological development
and the operation of SIAFI, the secure storage and the integrity of data, and the
maintenance of the system.
14.   SIAFI - Financial manatiement Functions. From a functional standpoint, SIAFI's
various subsystems allow for on-line recording, posting and processing of:
(a) budget execution transactions originating in federal government spending units
throughout the country;
(b) the deposit of tax and other federal cash revenues in the treasury's unified account held
at the Central Bank, and budget classification of collected revenues;
(c) payments to suppliers of goods & services and other parties, as well as transfers
between government units. All payments are made from the treasury's unified account
at the Central Bank, using Banco do Brazil as a paying agent;
(d) federal transfers to states and municipalities, whether mandatory or voluntary
(mandatory transfers to local governments are established by the Brazilian Constitution
and are calculated and paid by Banco do Brazil from balances in the treasury's unified
account, on the basis of a percentage of actual collection of certain taxes and a
system of distribution coefficients).  The system permits temporary blocking of
transfers when a local government is in non-compliance of its financial obligations with
the federal government.



88
(e) public debt disbursements and payments (the system has tools to calculate outstandings,
amortization and interest payments, bank charges and commissions, etc.);
(f) transactions under the official credit operations system subsidizing mainly the
agricultural sector.
Upon entry of each transaction by the system, SIAFI will:
(a) automatically update balances of appropriations in the federal budget registering
commitments, accruals and payments;
(b) automatically post the corresponding accounting entries. Utilities of the system allow to
produce at anytime the federal government's interim financial statements and budget
execution statements, as well as formal closing statements at the end of each fiscal
period. SIAFI also includes a subsystem to input the financial statements of states and
municipalities in order to produce the consolidated financial statement of the Union.;
(c) automatically updates all other financial records, such as balances in the treasury's
unified account, debt outstandings, balances of mandatory and voluntary transfers to
states and municipalities, etc.
The system is based on the principle that a transaction is entered into the system a single
time, and that such single entry automatically produces all the corresponding budget,
financial and accounting entries. In order to cancel or modify a transaction entered into the
system a new transaction has to be entered in SIAFI, thus leaving a clear audit trail of any
such changes.
15.   As a management tool, SIAFI's functionality includes facilities for:
(a) programming the financial execution of the federal budget on the basis of (i) budget
programming prepared by the Ministry of Planning, and (ii) the Treasury's cash flow
estimates (financial programming);
(b) preparing and monitoring the MOF's own budget programming;
(c) managing and reconciling of the treasury's unified account held at the Central Bank and
of payments thereof by Banco do Brazil;
(d) making automatic payments under pre-established accounts receivable and accounts
payable schedules submitted by spending units (introduced in 1998, this is an optional
facility for spending units who can also enter their receivable and payment transactions
in the system individually, as they happen);
(e) daily validation and confirmation by spending unit managers of transactions and
documents entered into the system, and monthly validation and confirmation of the
system's automatic accounting entries thereon;
(f) monitoring the fulfillment of contract conditions by states, municipalities, foundations
and other entities that benefit from government funding, whether reimbursable or not.
(g) performance of detailed consultations by operational and management users, and for
preparing standardized and customized reports. It provides budget, financial and
operating information at various levels of consolidation, ranging from the federal level,
to individual ministries and other agencies, as well as per spending unit. Sectorial



89
information by region, economic or functional sector, programs, projects, etc. can also
be obtained, as well as detailed information on individual transactions. Also, the system
permits the extraction of blocks of information from its data base for importation by
other systems and applications (e.g. spreadsheets), for analysis purposes.
In addition, the system offers adequate on-line help facilities for operational users, also
making available special training modules. Specifically there is (a) an on-line educational
version of SIAFI used for the training of operating and management staff and to support
public administration programs at universities, (b) a tutorial version, for self-paced
learning, in CD/ROM format, and (c) a SIAFI Manual, which is available on-line for all
users of the system.
16.   The SIAFI's system-administration modules provide for comprehensive access, data
transfer, data integrity and data storage security, as well as for maintenance of internal
administrative and data base tables supporting the operation of the system.  The system
includes audit facilities which constantly monitor and evaluate the integrity of its internal
processes. Due to its aging development technology and frequent modifications over its 13
year life span, documentation of the system is reported as not being as comprehensive as it
should be. However the system has on-line help facilities for users.
17.   The SIAFI version for managers (SIAFI Gerencial) is mainly a data consultation
and retrieval system, which provides managers user-friendly access to information stored in
the operational version's data base by way of standardized formats or customized reporting
facilities. As SIAFI Gerencial was developed using more modern technology than the
SIAFI Operacional version (it was developed in windows/based graphic mode, whereas the
operational version is developed with less friendly character mode) it provides managers
with much more flexibility and efficiency in the manipulation of information according to
their own needs. SIAFI Gerencial is not intended for registration of data but solely for
consultation and reporting functions.
18.   SIAFI - Technological Platform. The two versions of SIAFI currently in use have
different technological platforms, as the production version was developed several years
earlier than its management version.
SIAFI production version
19.   From a technological standpoint, the production version (SIAFI Operacional) runs
on a centralized mainframe platform system based on an IBM processor 9672-R46 and 4
2/4 MB 447 MIBS processors located in Brasilia. Users throughout Brazil are connected
to the mainframe facility either through PC/emulators using TCP/TN 3270 protocol, or
through terminals connected to IBM 3X74 processors and a SNA network using a
SNA/LU2.1 protocol. The SIAFI Operacional data base is ADABAS 15 BDs, with 650
Gigabytes. The transactional environment is CICS and the development language is
NATURAL, though other languages such as Predic, Roscoe, Adabas, Cobol and Cics have
also been used for development. In the case of some functional subsystems that are
integrated to SIAFI, such as the control of assets and liabilities and the monitoring of fiscal
information from states and municipalities, spreadsheet applications or less robust
databases are used, including Access, Paradox, etc. The size of SIAFI Operacional's



90
present data base is 60 GB. The mean response time of SIAFI Operacional is 2.0s. Other
operating indicators have been provided in Table A.7.3.
SIAFI management version
20.   In its management version (SIAFI Gerencial), the system is based on a client-server
platform with a centralized Oracle data base of 13GB, running on a central Digital
processor in Brasilia. The application was developed using Oracle CASE tools and it
operates in a Windows environment. Users can access the system through the internet
using TCP/SQLNET protocols. Users PC's have FORMS/EXCELL facilities.
Telecommunications platform
21.   Both SIAFI systems (production and management versions) are supported by a vast
telecommunications network, outreaching approximately 5,000 spending units throughout
the country, as outlined in Box A6.2.
22.   Telecommunications services for SIAFI users are offered by SERPRO, a business
unit of the MOF, which is also responsible for the operation and maintenance of the
computing systems on which SIAFI runs. From its central mainframe facility in Brasilia,
the SIAFI system outreaches 6,650 spending units throughout the country by way of
SERPRO's nationwide telecommunications arrangements using the infrastructure of several
domestic data transmission services, which range from X-25 and X-28 to more advanced
Frame Relay and ATM technology, permitting links between networks using diverse
telecommunications protocols. The headquarters of federal agencies and other users in
Brasilia can access SERPRO's virtual network through Telebrasilia's high speed network.
As of September 2000, SERPRO's network arrangements had 140,000 registered users in
700 municipalities throughout the country, linking 670 local networks and 200 external
networks, serving 55,000 terminals, PC's and printers. Web arrangements can handle
40,000 simultaneous internet connections. SERPRO bills its telecommunication services to
users of SIAFI, and in turn has billing arrangements with diverse telecommunications
carriers.



91
Box A6.2. SIAFI -Telecommunications Network

-F; p - ;  ; -V.1 1

both, technological and functional factors:
Technological assessment
24.   As an integrated financial management system (IFMS). SIAFI is an aging but still
performiing application, which accurately stores, processes and integrates operational
information recorded by spending units throughout the country, allowing the MOF/STN to
control the execution of the federal budget approved by Congress; to manage cash
resources and payments (including public debt payments) through the unified treasury
account at the central bank; to administer entries in the general accounting system of the
federal government;, and, to produce the consolidated financial statements of the Union. It
is also a valuable automated source of information for budget formulation and
programmning by the MP through the SIDOR system, and more recently for its monitoring
of program-based multi-annual planning (PPA) through the SIG  system.   As a
technological system STAFI plays an important role not only in providing accurate and



92
timely information to government managers at all levels, but is also instrumental in terms
of public sector fiscal transparency. However, after 13 years in operation, the system is
aging in technological terms, and its overall maintenance, both functionally and
techonologically, is increasingly cumbersome, inflexible, time-consuming and costly. Main
shortcomings are as follows:
(a) SIAFI's aging architecture does not facilitate the introduction of the advanced levels of
flexibility and agility in data processing required to satisfy an increasingly complex
financial management environment, thus the system is beginning to lag behind in terms
of information integration and analysis capabilities, as well as in relation to more
recently developed government systems, such as SIDOR and SIG, with which it has to
interact;
(b) Being of a centralized mainframe architecture, SIAFI in its present form does not allow
the introduction of more efficient data processing and telecommunication models
offering substantial efficiency gains and operating economies, such as a multi-layer
architecture for the differentiated management of the data base, the application and user
interfaces, which would provide the type of flexibility normally required by a large
modern financial management system with an scope comparable to that of as SIAFI.
(c) SIAFI was not developed with currently used techniques and integrated tools, such as
CASE based design and development, which permit automatic generation of program
codes, the efficient structuring of data bases, the introduction of extensive
parametrization facilities, and thorough documentation of the system, these being
features which reduce the time, risk and cost of modifications to adapt the system to
constant changes observed in financial management rules and processes.
(d) SIAFI was not developed in a Windows graphic environment, which provides greater
user-friendly interfaces and graphic capabilities.
In summary, in its present form and notwithstanding it is assessed as a solid and reliable
system, SIAFI represents for the Brazilian government a very high and rapidly increasing
risk of technological obsolescence for its main financial management system, as well as
very high maintenance costs into the future.
Functional assessment
25.   Since its implementation in 1986, SIAFI has been subject to constant modifications
and additions, responding to changes in financial management rules and operating
requirements in Brazil.  Between 1988 and 1999, SIAFI has had to continuously
accommodate a considerable number of major structural and operational changes, as well
as functional additions. Some of these developments were caused by changes in financial
management rules and procedures and others to improve services provided by the system in
response of user demand. This constant evolution of SIAFI and the resulting overlapping
patches in the system have added operational and structural complexities not anticipated in
the original design, and have thus weakened its integrity as a system and dispersed its
development documentation, increasing maintenance risks and costs. There is significant
and diversified demand from users for increased and/or improved functionality and for
more flexibility in information management that cannot be satisfied because of the
architectural rigidity of the system, which was designed as a large centralized mainframe



93
system accessible only by way terminals and developed in a programming language that
has been technologically overcome and can not offer Windows and graphics capabilities
which are currently commonplace.
26.   Functionally, SIAFI is presently facing the challenge to accommodate four major
new developments in fiscal/financial management in Brazil, namely:
(a) The introduction of program-based multiannual planning (PPA);
(b) The enactment and implementation of the Fiscal Responsibility Law (LFR);
(c) New institutional arrangements for debt management; and,
(d) New institutional arrangements for assets/liability management.
27.   The current SIAFI was designed to manage the information flows of a traditional
budgeting process, focused on funding the annual requirements of bureaucratic
administrative structures and of capital investment projects, rather than, as presently
required, on the funding of multi-annual programs and on the allocational and technical
efficiency of public expenditure based on strategic priorities and targeted outputs and
outcomes.
28.   Accommodatinif the PPA. A major fiscal reform presently underway, the PPA,
aims at making program-based multi-annual planning and budgeting more relevant,
operational, and effective, thus creating the need for a financial management system that
allows program costing, as well as performance and evaluation on a multi-annual basis.
The SIAFI system needs to be upgraded to accommodate this new focus of the PPA, as its
present data base structure is based on annual fiscal years rather than on multi-annual
planning. It is not specifically designed for tracking and linking expenditures to the pursuit
of program objectives. The new system must be able to allocate current and capital
expenditures to program categories and not only to agencies and their administrative units,
so that the cost and the performance of each of the 388 programs composing the PPA may
be determined and evaluated in relation to pre-established indicators and targets (e.g.
reduction in infant mortality to specified levels).
While SIAFI transactional codes have been modified to accommodate the PPA's new
program structures compromises had to be reached in order not to increase the aggregate
number of coding digits, which would have represented major and costly structural changes
in SIAFI's data base due to its aging technology. Tracking the physical execution of
programs with SIAFI as per PPA performance monitoring and evaluation requirements
would require the introduction of major changes in SIAFI data base and data capture
structures, which is a costly proposition if applied to a system with high obsolescence risks.
29.   Accommodatin2 the LFR. Under the LFR, the federal government as well as the
state and municipal governments, are required to establish multi-annual (3-years) fiscal
targets upon formulating their annual budget proposals. The LFR also establishes ceilings
on the ratio of personnel expenditures to net revenues. Additionally, the Executive Branch
has submitted to Congress legislative initiatives to establish maximum ratios between net
debt and net current revenues, as well as between gross bonded debt to net current
revenues. These initiatives are expected to be approved. Furthermore, under the LFR the



94
federal and local governments are required to disclose and widely disseminate information
on   public accounts, public debt, budget implementation, and fiscal management
performance, which imposes additional and more effective monitoring than that currently
possible through SIAFI, in particular with respect to its accounting consolidation facilities
whereby the union's consolidated financial statements are prepared.
30.   Accommodatin2 new institutional arrangements for debt mana2ement. While the
functionality of the current SIAFI includes the recording and processing of public debt
transactions, and the automatic posting of accounting entries thereon, the system does not
provide for effective debt management in an environment where new structured debt
models and instruments appear with increasing frequency in the international and domestic
capital markets. The government is presently undertaking a reform of its debt management
systems, as well as specific actions to centralize debt management functions transferring
them to the STN. Among other issues, this implies the development of a more solid debt
informnation system to satisfy the operating requirements of the new back, middle and front
offices for debt management, which implies the replacement SIAFI's current debt
management modules.
31. AccommodatinR new institutional arrangements for asset/liabilitv management.
Similarly, the government is making efforts to gain better control over the recording and
the flow of its assets and liabilities on an integral basis, and effort that will fall under the
purview of the STN. This functionality is not included in the current SIAFI and its
introduction involves the automation of new institutional arrangements within the STN to
manage an assets/liabilities portfolio in the amount of approximately of US$ 185 and 335
billion, respectively.
32.  In summary, these technological and functional considerations strongly support the
notion that the current and aging SIAFI must be replaced with a more modern, flexible, and
functionally upgraded integrated financial management application which properly
addresses the new policies and institutional arrangements for public sector financial
management, and that may also interact more efficiently with other government systems
that use more modem technology.
THE SUFl 21st Century PROPOSAL
33.   Proiect background and mission. Since 1999 the Brazilian federal government is
developing efforts to replace SIAFI with a more advanced system both, functionally and
technologically. This project is known as SIAFI 21St Century, and falls under the
responsibility of the MOF, and in particular the STN. The project's mission has been
defined as "the adequation of SIAFI to the new paradigms of public management, adding
functionalities and promoting the modernization of its technological environment, aiming at
more effectivity in the administration of assets and liabilities of the national treasury, as
well as in the budgetary, financial and patrimonial administration of the federal
government". The SIAFI 21St Century project is expected to be implemented in 3 years,
beginning January 2001. Between 2001 and 2003 the various functional modules or
subsystems of the new SIAFI application will be gradually developed and will be
implemented and become operational as they are completed. Capital investment for



95
hardware and software modernization will take place mainly during the first two years of
the project.
34.   Expected benefits. The project aims at adapting the functionality of SIAFI to the
new financial management model of the federal government, which establishes program-
based multi-annual planning (PPA), and calls for more operational integration between
planning, budgeting, treasury, debt management and asset/liability management, thus
replacing the historical bureaucratic public administration model with a management model
supporting productivity and results. To achieve this, the project would incorporate new
management approaches and techniques that are conceptually absent in the current SIAFI,
such as program-based multi-annual planning; monitoring and evaluation of the physical
and financial execution of the budget from a results-oriented management perspective
rather than only from an accounting perspective; costing of government outputs and
outcomes, enhanced public debt and asset/liability   management; and, improved
accountability at the federal and local government levels. The project also aims at
improving SIAFI's capabilities to interact with other government systems and with other IT
applications and tools used by government managers to perform their daily functions. The
project also aims at modernizing the administration of the STN, providing it with advanced
information management and workflow tools for the control of its operations and
documents.
35.   Specific benefits expected from the SIAFI 21st Century system can be summarized
as follows:
(a) 24 hours per day, seven days per week availability of the system;
(b) Increase and effective maximization of the number of simultaneous users;
(c) Increase in the system's capacity to integrate information and handle large volumes of
data;
(d) Windows-based multi-task environment with graphic user interface and WEB
philosophy;
(e) Friendly interface, in Portuguese;
(f) A system more suited to satisfy the specific needs of each type of user, and providing
user-oriented services, including the availability of spread sheets, word processors, text
editors, graphics and imaging, statistical functions, projections and simulations, help
desk, etc.
(g) Flexibility and agility for user-specified performance of data analysis and of analysis
refinements at various levels of complexity, including facilities for statistical analysis,
projections and scenario simulations;
(h) Significant reduction in maintenance costs, in particular for functional customization
and the incorporation of changes in the legal framework, rules of business,
functionalities, etc.;
(i) On-line documentation and help;
(j) Ease and agility in data entry and retrieval;

(k) Increased ease and agility for data export and import;

(s) Availability of daily balances for all types of transactions and accounts;

(y) Capacity to monitor compliance of the Law for Fiscal Responsibility by entities at the
federal and local government levels;
(z) Accounting of the fiscal performance of the national treasury;

(a) Budgetary, financial and patrimonial administration;
(b) Administration of assets and liabilities;
(c) States and municipalities oversight; and,
(d) Internal administration of the STN.

38.   Project preparation activities.  While many of the financial management
processes and business rules are already immersed in the current SIAFI and will be
migrated to the new application, since mid-2000 the STN has formed a number of project
preparation workgroups that are perforrning process and procedures analysis tasks in
various areas. One of these groups is analyzing since august 2000 all the internal workflow
of the treasury for the financial planning of budget execution. Two other groups are
performing similar work since October 2000 in the assets and liabilities and debt
management areas.  In parallel, joint STN/SERPRO  technological workgroups are



99
performing analysis in the system security area and for the selection of design and
development tools. These efforts involve a team of 16 individuals in STN staff and 4
technicians from SERPRO.  Project preparation activities presently include training
programs for STN and SERPRO information technicians in CASE-based design and
development tools that are expected to be used in the project. Three external consultants
are working with SERPRO for the use of RATIONAL development and evaluation tools
and project monitoring tools.
39.   Additionally, SERPRO has formed a team for the selection and homologation of the
information technology platform (h/w, s/w and data base) that will be used for SIAFI 21St
Century, and preliminary proposals are presently being considered.  An structured
technological validation program has been initiated with regard to the three-layer system
architecture being proposed (the data layer; the application layer and the user interface
layer). Pilots for each layer have been developed and tested with the participation of
relevant potential suppliers including Rational, Compuware, Microsoft, Oracle, Sun, IBM,
Silicon Graphics and Compaq. The technological validation program further includes areas
such as: system solutions, integration with other technologies, tools for the administration
and monitoring of the production environment, system escalation and data warehouse
technologies. The results of these validation processes will determine final technological
choices pursuant to further technical and commercial analysis. Strategies for the use of the
chosen technologies and for their implementation are also being developed. System and
access security are critical areas under the validation process, and include among other
the integration of firewalls, the use of SERPRO's virtual private network, and a Web
applications allowing the incorporation of digital signatures. At the end of these processes
SNT and SERPRO intend to seek digital security certification from a widely recognized
certification agency (CA).
40.   Therefore, notwithstanding project implementation did not begin in January 2000 as
originally expected, STN and SERPRO have made significant progress in project
preparation, and the STN expects to complete the technological validation program and
make its final technological choices by the second Quarter of 2001.
41.   As an important part of project preparation activity and technical and financial
schedules for the project have been developed, and funding required for the first year of its
implementation has been included in the 2001 federal budget proposal that Congress is due
to approve by December 15, 2000, thus allowing the beginning of the project in January
2001, which would permit to substantially complete the project by 2003.
42.   Proposed project implementation schedule. Table 7.4.7 summarizes the proposed
2201-2003 project schedule, by Quarter. Subsystems will be implemented and become
operative as their development and the training of users is completed. The three-year life
span of the project is justified by the STN and SERPRO in terms of the time required not
only for the development of the new SIAFI application, but also for the evaluation of
platform alternatives and state-of-the-art technologies; training of IT resources in the use of
new system development technologies and tools, possibly including object-oriented
programming; the introduction of a new system for the management of the project; and,
the  competitive procurement of goods and services for the implementation of the



100
development, homologation and production environments, much of which has to achieved
before actual development and implementation begin.
43.   On the other hand, the implementation schedule of the SIAFI 21St Century project
also takes into account its timely insertion in the government's Brasil Trasparente
program, aiming at increased public expenditure transparency; the need to co-ordinate
actions so that gradual implementation coincides with budget and fiscal cycles; the
convenience of completing the project before the current administration's leaves office in
2003; and, the existing urgency to reduce the technological and financial management risks
represented by the aging current SIAFI system.

44.   Project preparation during 2000 included technology evaluation tasks, system
architecture design and training of STN and SERPRO technicians in the use of



101
development tools, which will allow development of the various subsystem from the
beginning of 2001.
45.   The development and implementation of the budget, financial and patrimonial
subsystems is tied to the federal budget preparation schedule, thus the budget planning and
formulation modules will be given development and implementation priority in 2001 so
that they become available by February 2002, in time for training users before the
beginning of the preparation of the 2003 budget proposal. The STN reports that the reason
why the SIAFI 21st Century includes a number of budget formulation and planning
functions which would normally correspond to the MP's budget system, is that the SIDOR
network outreaches to around 700 budget units only, while SIAFI's network expands to
4,560 spending units (UG for Unidades de Gestao or management units), providing them
with system capabilities to undertake basic budgeting functions that supports the MP's
overall budgeting requirements. For the same reason, the new SIAFI modules would also
include modules to register physical execution of the budget at the spending unit level,
catering to information requirements of program managers under the PPA.
46.   Notwithstanding careful planning of the SIAFI 21st Century project, its
implementation schedule remains extremely ambitious, not so much in terms of the
estimated duration of the development of each subsystem, but in terms of the concurrent
development and implementation of two very major subsystems: the budget, financial and
patrimonial subsystem and the assets & liabilities management subsystem, in parallel to the
development of less complex subsystems for local government oversight and for the
internal administration of the STN. In order to mitigate implementation delays, the STN
and SERPRO are planning to assign to the SIAFI-21t Century project technical resources
who are presently operating SIAFI and are thus very familiar with its functionality and day-
to-day operation, with the expectation that this will facilitate and expedite the development
of the new system. As the present SIAFI would continue to operate while the new system
is being developed and operating, the strategy is to hire and train new technical resources
for its operation. Extremely strong and effective overall project management will be
required for the execution and timely completion of the SIAFI- 21St Century project. The
STN is welcoming Bank support in this area under a technical assistance proposal which
would include one top IT expert to advise on technological choices at the initial stage of the
project, one senior consultant to provide project management support throughout the life of
the project and one senior financial management specialist to assist in the integration of
budget and treasury functions. In summary, project execution should be closely monitored
to ensure its successful and timely execution.



102
47.   Proposed proiect budget and financial schedule. Table A6.4  summarizes the
project's budget between 2001 and 2003. STN officials with whom this budget has been
discussed have expressed the view that it is still a high-level estimation, and that actual
project costs are likely to be significantly lower. The suggestion was made that recent
costing refinements after initial valuation of technological alternatives seem to confirm this
view. On the other hand, in a project of the scope of SIAFI 21 st Century is can be expected
that once the project is underway user demands for additional functionalities and facilities
are likely to result in increased investment and development costs. In the course of the
preparation of this Annex various budget versions were reviewed which showed variations
in a range up to 20% in large certain budget components. The budget versions differed in
terms of cost elements and their grouping, making comparisons and interpretation difficult.
However, the budget provided in Table A6.4 is an adequate working-premise that is close
to what has reportedly been included in the 2001 budget proposal for project infrastructure
and application development.
High development cost
48.   The budgeted costs for the development and implementation of the SIAFI 21 t
Century system appear to be very high in relation to other known Latin-American
experiences for the development of integrated financial management systems. The more
relevant would appear to be the Argentine and Mexican IFMS development projects,
though system and deployment and scopes would no doubt show significant variances. The
budget for SIAFI 21st Century includes US $ 15.3 million solely for the creation of a
development environment in SERPRO, to which additional US $ 15.4 million have been
added for direct application-development costs. At US $ 30.8 million in development and
training costs, before capital investments of US $ 33.4 million for the creation of permanent
production, training, telecommunications and information management environments,
there is no major evidence that the use of SERPRO as technological partner of the project
represents significant cost advantages to the Ministry of Finance. It appears that an
important capitalization of SERPRO has been included in the US $ 64.2 million budget
for the SIAFI 21st Century project, whereas such capitalization could have been treated
separately in order to identify and evaluate direct project costs. Taking these observations
into consideration, the role and cost of SERPRO as the technological partner of the
MOF/STN should perhaps been compared with competitive market alternatives at least for
the application-development stage of the project.  Such analysis falls beyond the scope of
this Annex, thus consideration should be given to independent external validation of the
budget being proposed for the SIAFI 21st Century project. This validation is a possible
component of the TA loan under preparation that will accompany the implementation of the
program supported by the PFRSAL.

49.   In addition to its very high cost, there are a number of other concerns with respect
to the estimated budget of the SIAFI 21 st Century Project:
Financing of the proiect's budget

appropriations of approximately US $ 20 million to finance the creation of the

applications or subsystems, but does not include the capital investments portion of the
budget, which amounts to more than US $ 33 million. Reportedly, capital investment

funding would be raised by STN during project execution by way of additional credits to
be incorporated in the federal budget. Also, SERPRO would reportedly raise its share of
capital expenditures by way of a loan from the federal government or supported by the it.

amount of US $ 34.5 million required for the creation of production-related environments
